Silk and Satin Guild Resolves Measures to Eliminate Industry Disputes 140

All Retailers Unanimously Stamp and Abide

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Silk and Satin Trade Association of this city believes that the national silk industry is declining day by day, and disputes among fellow merchants are intensifying. The association, mindful of the difficult times and taking the environment into consideration, believes that if these issues are not resolved quickly, the endangered national silk industry will fall into a state of irreversible ruin. Therefore, in accordance with Article 4, Paragraph 3 of the association's charter, and at the request of the members, in order to seek a fair solution, it has united the Electrical Machinery Silk Weaving Factory Trade Association and the representatives of other companies and businesses to form a special supplementary committee to eliminate disputes and revive the national silk industry. After several meetings and consultations, an outline of the measures was first determined and submitted to the Third Second Joint Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the association for revision and approval. The three articles of the preliminary measures were notified to all retail merchants for unified compliance, and they were ordered to affix their seals to each household to acknowledge and abide by them permanently. The association has already distributed the notification to each retail merchant for their seals. It is now known that Lao Jiefu, Lao Jiuhe, Lao Jiulun, Lixingxiang, Dalun, Dachang, Dacheng, Daxin, Tianfu, Xincheng, Hongxiangtai, Zhuang Tongshun, Yu Deji, Liyang, Tianxiang, Hongzhang, Hongda, Lao Jingfu, Cheng Jinzhang, Dajing, Zhengtai, Lao Jiafu, Zhenda, Tianjin, Yushun, Tongshun, Yu…, Deda, Dashengfu, Tianwan, Sanyi, Dahua, Dakang Xieji, Yuxin, Tianlun, Tianfeng, Lao Jielun, He Changlan, Hengfeng, Za Da, Dazheng, Minghua, Meilun, and other silk and satin shops, as well as Huahua and Shanghai silk and satin companies, and Yongan, Sincere, New Asia, China National Products, Shanghai National Products, Lihua, and other silk departments have all signed and stamped their approval of the three articles of the preliminary outline. Yesterday, the reporter interviewed Mr. Luo Qinghua, chairman of the association, who spoke about the recent situation of the silk and satin industry and the future rescue measures, and showed a copy of the association's announcement signed and stamped by fifty-one silk and satin shops and companies, which is transcribed as follows:

Mr. Luo's speech: Mr. Luo Qinghua, a supervisory committee member of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, has been in the silk and satin business for many years. This autumn, he was elected as the chairman of the Silk and Satin Trade Association and is well aware of the situation in the industry. The reporter made a special visit to the Silk Industry Bank, where Mr. Luo told him that everyone knows that silk and satin are special products of China with a long and glorious history. Since neighboring countries have begun to imitate them and replace hand-made goods with machine-made goods, the production is fast and the quality is excellent. As a result, the overseas market of national silk has been gradually taken over, and foreign silk imports have almost become the main product. Fortunately, Chinese silk merchants have begun to catch up, buying machines and striving for improvement. Since the emergence of Chinese silk gauze, imported wild silk gauze has no market. In recent years, factories have been able to study carefully, and the technology has become more sophisticated. The products have shown obvious progress. Chinese silk factories can make almost all kinds of silk and satin that can be made in Eastern and Western countries. China has been advocating machine-made goods for nearly 30 years, and the silk and satin industry has made great progress. Chinese people are also becoming more aware of the need to use domestic goods. With these factors, the silk and satin industry should become more prosperous. However, due to the impact of the recent economic downturn, both domestic and foreign sales have become narrow. The machine-made goods is faster than the hand-made goods. Silk and satin merchants, due to the market downturn and difficulty in selling, are rushing to lower prices and compete to sell. Now, merchants in the same industry are undercutting each other more and more fiercely. Some are even disregarding their cost and using radio broadcasts and newspapers to promote cheap goods. If this continues, manufacturers will inevitably cut corners to suit market prices. In general, consumers only care about the low price and don't ask about the quality when they buy. After wearing the clothes, they complain that the quality of domestic goods is not good and use this as an excuse to buy foreign goods. The impact of this is actually significant. The purpose of the three articles of the outline agreed upon by the Silk and Satin Trade Association this time is to correct these malpractices. On the one hand, it wants to enable silk and satin merchants to strive for meager profits in a proper way. On the other hand, it also wants to enable consumers to buy genuine domestic silk and not be overwhelmed by excessive advertising. Now, this outline has been signed and stamped by retail silk and satin shops and companies, and has legally become a contractual act. It is expected that everyone will be able to abide by it and not deviate from it. Mr. Luo also said that he is now working with the Lake Society to prepare for a national silk exhibition. The aim is to promote the advantages of national silk and promote the psychology of using it. It is expected that it can be held at the Lake Society during the Lunar New Year.

Public Announcement by the Association: Respected Sirs, the national silk business has been declining year by year, and efforts to save it have been ineffective. Disputes among fellow merchants have also intensified. The association, mindful of the difficult times and taking the environment into consideration, believes that if these issues are not resolved quickly, the endangered national silk business will fall into a state of irreversible ruin. Therefore, in accordance with the provisions of Article 4, Item 2 of the association's charter, and at the request of the members, in order to seek a fair solution, it has united the Electrical Machinery Silk Weaving Factory Trade Association and the representatives of other companies and businesses to form a special committee to eliminate disputes and revive the silk industry. After several meetings and consultations, the three articles of the preliminary measures were determined and submitted to the association for deliberation and implementation. The three articles of the preliminary measures have now been revised and approved by the First Joint Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Third Association and notified to all retail merchants for unified compliance, and they have been ordered to affix their seals to each household to acknowledge and abide by them permanently. The preliminary measures are recorded as follows: 1. Merchants are in business to make a profit of ten percent. The selling price of silk and satin is usually at least ten percent higher. 2. The right to set prices is controlled by the manufacturers. 3. No slander or depreciation of other people's goods is allowed. That is, prices cannot be advertised on radio broadcasts. The association believes that the above three measures are indeed essential for our industry to turn decline into prosperity, and retail merchants should not neglect to understand this and abide by it together. As for the friendship between merchants, we have always valued harmony, but as a result of excessive competition in business, there have been facts such as the closure of factories and the suspension of Laojiuhe silk goods. The association deeply regrets this. From now on, the retail group's business policies will have rules to follow. Colleagues should know that the national situation is in danger, the silk industry is declining, and we must work together to seek common survival and prosperity. The misunderstanding with Laojiuhe in the past should be resolved as soon as possible to restore the harmony between the client and restore the prosperity of the silk industry. This association has high expectations for this and hereby announces it.

Reasons for Using English Yards and Pounds in Foreign Trade 141

Requests Submitted by Silk and Electrical Machinery Associations

Instructions from the Ministry of Industry Have Been Approved

The two trade associations of silk and satin merchants and electrical machinery silk weaving factories in this city believe that since their members have followed the new market foot and market scale, in terms of foreign trade, only by using the English yard and pound can foreign merchants be convinced. Therefore, they wrote to the International Trade Bureau to forward to the Ministry of Industry the reasons for the need to prepare English yards and pounds, requesting approval. Now, they have received a reply from the International Trade Bureau stating that, "The reasons you submitted earlier for using the English yard and pound in foreign trade have been investigated and are indeed valid. We have immediately signed an opinion, stating that if any merchant belonging to the two trade associations is fined for having yards and pounds in their accounts, the two trade associations can convert the length of the yard and the weight of the pound into market feet and market catties. However, the conversion must be based on the standards stipulated in the 'Chinese and Foreign Weights and Measures Conversion Table' compiled by the Ministry. The two trade associations should also create a conversion table between yards and pounds and meters and kilograms, and notify their members to follow it. After any store or factory in the two industries trades with foreign merchants, the number of yards and pounds of the goods sold should be converted into market feet and market catties and recorded in the accounts. In this way, all difficulties and disputes can be resolved invisibly." We have submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry for approval. Now, we have received Directive No. 10678 from the Ministry of Industry, stating that, "We have received your request and have temporarily approved the proposed method. However, the members of each association should first submit the method and the number of English yard and pound instruments they have prepared to the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for verification and record. Please instruct them to comply with this order." Based on this, we have specially forwarded the details of the handling to your association and hope that you will investigate and notify your members to comply. In accordance with the letter, the two trade associations immediately reprinted the "Chinese and Foreign Weights and Measures Conversion Table" compiled by the Ministry and created a conversion table between yards and pounds and meters and kilograms, which were recorded and distributed to each of their members, along with the letter and directive, for unified compliance. The number of English yard and pound instruments to be prepared by each member was also submitted to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for record.

Four Threatening Letters Demanding Extortion of Three Thousand Yuan 148

Detectives Disguised for Contact

One Bandit Arrested

Rong Jiadao, the Ningbo native owner of Xieheshun Paper and Incense Shop at 225 Seward Road, suddenly received four threatening letters from bandits between the 4th and 19th of last month. The first letter contained a bullet, demanding 1,500 yuan. The subsequent three letters increased the demand to 3,000 yuan, initially arranging contact at the Great World, Small World, and the Jingju (Peking Opera) and Changzhou Tanhuang (local opera) sections of the amusement park. Otherwise, they threatened to resort to violent means, posing a danger to his life. After receiving the letters, Rong was extremely frightened and reported the matter to the Hongkou Police Station. Detectives Wang Runhe, Bai Mingfu, and others were dispatched to the arranged locations for an arrest, but to no avail. The last letter arranged a meeting at Room 8 of the Shuixing Hotel in the French Concession's Eight Immortals Bridge area to deliver the money. Someone was to come and collect it. The victim sent his representative, Xue Changgui, with a leather suitcase containing mock banknotes from the "Ming Dynasty Bank," with one genuine ten-yuan banknote from the Zhongnan Bank wrapped in the middle to resemble 3,000 yuan. Xue was accompanied by detectives Wang and Bai, disguised as travelers. Yesterday afternoon, they first went to a room opposite Room 8 of the hotel to wait. At around 11 o'clock, they saw a man in a black cotton-padded jacket and trousers arrive and enter Room 8. Xue Changgui, carrying the suitcase with the agreed-upon signal, and detectives Wang and Bai rushed forward, arresting him. Upon interrogation, he was identified as Xie Caixi, a native of Shaoxing, and taken back to the police station for detention. This morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Tribunal of the First Special Court. Mr. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, detailed the prior events, requesting an adjournment. The letters were presented for examination. Subsequently, victim Rong Jiadao and witness Xue Changgui testified to the course of events. Defendant Xie Caixi confessed that he was acting on the instructions of a fugitive named Gen Sheng. Judge Wu Zihan, after deliberation, ordered him to be remanded in custody for further verification.

Industrial and Commercial Management Association Releases One-Year Work Overview 152

The Chinese Industrial and Commercial Management Association recently released an overview of its annual work, stating: "In response to social needs, this association was established in July of the 19th year (of the Republic) by Minister Kong and Shanghai's industrial and commercial leaders, and it has been five years since. All matters concerning the research and investigation of scientific management, as well as the collection of data and editing of books, have been carefully planned and actively implemented, with the hope of achieving practical results as soon as possible and contributing to our industrial and commercial sectors. However, the association's funding has been quite strained, leading to a regrettable slow progress in the implementation of its initiatives, and making it difficult to fully realize the planned projects. The association's funding sources, besides the annual membership fees paid by members, rely entirely on subsidies from the government for maintenance. Fortunately, in recent years, efforts have been made to economize, and the funding has been somewhat sufficient, allowing all work to gradually progress. The work of the past year is briefly reported as follows: 1. Publishing Projects: Scientific management is rapidly advancing in advanced countries, and the achievements of its implementation steps can serve as a valuable reference for us. Therefore, in addition to translating and compiling famous works from the East and West to introduce to the people, the association also publishes the Industrial and Commercial Management Monthly, which mainly contains expert articles and can be considered the only publication in China dedicated to the study of management science. 2. Cultivating Management Talent: For all operations, talent is of utmost importance, and cultivating management talent is a pressing need for today's industrial and commercial sectors. Therefore, in addition to jointly running the Scientific Management Training Class with the Business School of Shanghai University, the association has also opened an Industrial Management Training Class within the association, starting with intermediate-level talents. Preparations are also underway to open an Industrial and Commercial Management Evening School, dividing the classes into day and night sessions to teach various management sciences. Due to time constraints, it has been decided to start the school in the spring of next year. 3. Investigation and Guidance: The implementation of scientific management must first be based on facts. Those who take established rules and use them improperly will achieve no good results. Therefore, the association, on the one hand, investigates the actual management situation of various factories in Shanghai, conducting detailed inspections, analysis, and synthesis, using the results as a basis for individual contributions, so as to avoid the problem of 'cutting the feet to fit the shoes.' On the other hand, a service department is specially established, stipulating two methods: discussion, reporting, and reorganization, for factories to adopt and implement improvements. Significant benefits have been achieved in their implementation and guidance. For example, after the association's guidance to the Watson Electric Appliance Factory, the factory's production volume has increased significantly compared to before. This has attracted the attention of other factories, and some have already requested the association to guide and improve their management. If future financial resources are sufficient and achievements are evident, then the impact will likely spread, and there is great hope for the improvement of China's production industry. 4. Lectures and Discussions: Scientific management involves countless details. At this stage of advocacy, it is necessary to examine past achievements, observe current conditions, and conduct thorough discussions to establish the steps for implementing improved management. The association holds discussion and lecture meetings every month, inviting experts to lecture on various management methods and economic issues related to industry and commerce, and the lecture records are published in the monthly journal for the reference of all sectors. The above is a summary of the association's recent work. Future progress will depend on the needs of the environment and the availability of financial resources. It is also hoped that people from all walks of life and the government will provide strong support so that the association's endeavors can thrive and benefit industry and commerce. Would that not be fortunate for the association alone?"

British Cargo Ship Bankok Maru Arrives Safely in Shanghai After Burning Wood Instead of Coal 153

Successfully Completed a Risky Experiment During a Storm

The British cargo ship *Bankok Maru* arrived in Shanghai yesterday, fully loaded with timber, after traveling from Japan. It is reported that after departing from the United States, the ship encountered a severe storm, making the work of adding coal extremely difficult. Therefore, over 1,700 logs of timber carried on the ship were used as fuel. It took fourteen days of sailing from the Pullen Strait to reach Japan. The use of wood instead of coal on a sea vessel is something people talk about. Fortunately, the ship arrived safely in Shanghai, thanks to the efforts and daring of the crew.

Fire on Shandong Road: Three Women Injured, Two Dead, One Missing 160

Huaxing Sewing Shop Completely Destroyed

Gu's Jewelry Shop Employee's Body Burned Beyond Recognition

The Huaxing Sewing Shop at 144 Shandong Road, owned by Shen Xirong from Pudong, specializing in mosquito nets and pillowcases, caught fire at around 3:30 AM yesterday. Everyone in the shop was fast asleep, and the fire suddenly broke out in the cotton and fabric pile in the shop, but no one noticed. Therefore, the fire spread uncontrollably. By the time the people upstairs were awakened, it was already unstoppable. At the same time, neighbors were awakened from their dreams and hurriedly carried their belongings, helping the elderly and leading the young, fleeing in panic. The guests at the Lao Huizhong Hotel were even more panicked. Because it was the middle of the night, the fire caused great disturbance. Fortunately, the Central Fire Brigade was nearby and quickly dispatched fire trucks to put out the fire. It was quickly extinguished, but three women in the building were injured by the fire: Shen Xuerong, 29 years old, and Zhong Guixiang, 15 years old. The shop owner was also knocked unconscious by the smoke and unable to escape, resulting in his death by burning. After the fire, firefighters found his charred body among the rubble, in a gruesome state, and sent it to the coroner for examination. The entire shop was also reduced to ashes. After the incident, the police immediately investigated the cause of the fire for further investigation.

Severe Drought in Qidong: Officials and Gentry Come to Shanghai to Beg for Relief 163

Qidong is located north of the Yangtze River and east of the Yellow Sea. Last autumn, it was hit by a typhoon and tidal surge, which breached the dikes. Fortunately, charitable organizations and philanthropists in Shanghai generously provided aid, enabling tens of thousands of disaster victims to survive the winter and spring through emergency relief and work relief. Unexpectedly, this year's summer drought has been devastating, with many of the planted corn, cotton, and beans yielding no harvest in as many as 22 villages. The number of disaster victims awaiting relief is estimated to be over 80,000. County Magistrate Li Baojian and local gentry Zhu Chuliang, Zhang Shunru, Shi Wenfan, and Yan Jingzhi have come to Shanghai, together with the resident Shanghai representatives for begging for relief, Gu Nanqun and Gu Yueseng, to seek relief from charitable organizations such as the Chinese Jiji Relief Association, the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, the World Red Cross, and the provincial drought relief associations. They are busy running around all day.

No Fees Required for Water and Electricity Connections for Houses Built in the Central District 164

The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities, in response to a request from the Bureau of Public Works and the Central District Construction Committee regarding Shanghai Bank's complaint about Zhabei Water and Electricity Company demanding a temporary water connection fee of 270 yuan for residential buildings under construction on Zhengde East Road and Guojing Road in the central district, has ruled that since the water pipes in that area have already been designated by the municipal government for subsidized water connection, no additional fees are required. The Zhabei Water and Electricity Company responded that there was no such incident. Further inquiry from Shanghai Bank revealed that their information was based on a letter from land owner Yu Jinyu, who in turn stated that the information came from architect Hengyao Company. Hengyao Company then claimed that it was conveyed from the Lu Genji Construction Company. Subsequently, Lu Genquan, the owner of the construction company, came to the bureau and stated that he had never told the Hengyao Company that. He is now preparing to file a lawsuit according to law. The true nature of this case is unclear. Since the factory is about to file a lawsuit, the court should investigate and determine the truth. However, because this matter is of great importance, the bureau has published a notice in the newspaper to avoid any future misunderstandings, stating that all water and electricity construction in the central district is fully subsidized by the municipal government, and land owners building houses are not required to pay any fees for water and electricity connections, so that land owners in the district can pay attention and avoid being deceived.

Six Months Imprisonment for Throwing Manure 171

Ding Xiuying's Face Covered in Filth

Ding Xiuying, a 20-year-old woman from Yangzhou, was a worker at the Number Three Cotton Mill inside and outside of West Suzhou Road. At around 5:00 PM yesterday, she was returning home from the factory when a man suddenly appeared while she was walking on Yichang Road Bridge, having waited for her there. Upon seeing Ding, he threw a cigarette tin full of manure at her head, covering her face and body in filth and a pungent odor. The woman screamed. A nearby Chinese police officer, No. 2224, heard the scream and rushed over, apprehending the man. He, along with Ding, were brought back to the Putuo Road police station. Under investigation by Detective Chen Guangrong, it was revealed that the man was named Zhang A'er, from Jiangbei. He did not know Ding Xiuying. It turned out that another female worker from the same factory, Miss Jia, had a feud with Ding and had her brother, Lu A'da, pay Zhang four dimes to do it. Yesterday morning, the police station sent Zhang A'er to the Criminal Division Eight of the First Special District Local Court. The police station's lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, charged Zhang with violating Article 319 of the Criminal Law regarding the obstruction of freedom, and explained the circumstances. Judge Deng Baosun questioned both the plaintiff and the defendant. Since the facts were clear, he immediately rendered a verdict in court, sentencing Zhang A'er to six months of imprisonment as a warning.

Zhang Boren Accused of Beating His Wife 173

Zhang Boren, a 21-year-old Western doctor from Ningbo at No. 441 Guangxi Road, married a Miss Zhao in his hometown two years ago. Miss Zhao is one year younger than Zhang. After marriage, the couple had a strong affection for each other. Zhang was assigned to Shanghai for work, so he brought his elderly mother and beloved wife to live with him in the clinic. Soon, a son was born. However, Zhang developed the idea of abandoning his old wife. He ordered Zhao to move out of the clinic and frequently abused her. Zhang's mother also sided with her son against her daughter-in-law. As a result, a harmonious family turned into a place of quarrels. Every time Zhao was abused, she complained to the police station. The police chief always advised them to return home and settle things, as they were a married couple and mother-in-law. On the 14th of this month, Zhang and Zhao had another conflict. Zhang accused her of becoming too liberal after coming to Shanghai and wanted to force her to return to their hometown, while Zhao claimed that Zhang had her move out of the clinic to make it easier for him to have affairs with other women. They argued, then fought. Zhao was punched in the ear, causing injury. Zhao went to the Laozha Police Station with her child, reporting the situation of being beaten. Considering this incident was more serious than before, the police chief deemed it inappropriate to tolerate it any further and filed a lawsuit against Zhang Boren in the Second Special District Local Court for inflicting injury. Yesterday, Judge Huang Risheng summoned both parties. After questioning, he ordered the defendant to post a 200-yuan bond and rescheduled the trial.

Unsuccessful Job Search, Lost Investment; Introducer in Difficult Position 174

Forced to Write a Thousand-Yuan IOU

The Wang Yao Kun and Son Too Outrageous

Wang Yaokun, a 49-year-old man from Wuxi, used to run a distiller's shop in his hometown. His son, Wu Xiqing, had been unemployed for a long time, so he asked Chen Yitang, also from Wuxi, to recommend him for a job. Chen, the owner of the Wanyuan Money Shop behind the New World Hotel in Wuxi, introduced him to Dai Shengtan. Dai, in addition to his position at the Wing On Bank in Shanghai, also operated the Yongchang Gold Shop on the third floor of the Silk Industry Bank on Sanma Road, specializing in speculation. Dai promised to help with the job request when the Wing On Bank branch opened. However, Dai requested a purchase of the bank's stocks, valued at 1000 yuan. Wang, eager to get the job, sent 1000 yuan through his father, Yao Kun, in May. Wang Xiqing was temporarily placed in the Yongchang Gold Shop. Recently, Dai's speculation failed, and the Yongchang Gold Shop went bankrupt. Dai disappeared. Wang searched everywhere but could not find him. Not only did the promised job fall through, but also the 1000 yuan invested in stocks was lost. It was an intentional fraud. Because Chen Yitang was the introducer, Wang sought recourse from Chen. Fearing Chen would not come to Shanghai, Wu Xiqing made a long-distance phone call to Chen Yitang in Wuxi yesterday morning, falsely claiming that Dai Shengtan had been apprehended and asked Chen to come to Shanghai immediately. Chen was overjoyed, as he himself had been swindled out of 2000 yuan by Dai. He believed that now that he had been caught, it would be easier to recover the money, so he did not suspect any trickery. Chen rushed to Shanghai in the afternoon. Wang Xiqing met him at the station. Chen and Wang hired a rickshaw and went to 254 Antongqi in Hubei Road. Wang's father, Wang Yao Kun, was in the room as well. After a few minutes, four gangsters broke into the room and, joined by Wang and his father, threatened Chen and forced him to write an IOU for 1000 yuan. Chen, facing violence and helpless, had to write the IOU. After Chen left, he told his friend, Dr. Shen Mengxun, about the ordeal and asked for help. Shen and Chen caught Wang Yao Kun but the others got away. The police found the forced IOU, and imprisoned Wang. The police lawyer, Qian Xunjiu, presented the case to the First Special Court, accusing them of illegal detention under Article 318 of the Criminal Code. Chen Yitang testified that the 1000 yuan was given to Dai Shengtan. Wang Yao Kun claimed that the money was delivered to Chen Yitang on May 16th. He asked Jiang Yiping, lawyer, to present evidence. Judge Deng ordered the case adjourned for seven days for further hearing, and approved Wang Yao Kun's request to post a 500-yuan bond.

Pilot Petitioning Group Petitioned Xu Jixiang Yesterday 175

No Result as Xu Was in Beijing on Official Business

Banquet for Maritime Groups Requesting Assistance

The Shanghai and Hanzhong Joint Petitioning Group for Pilots, consisting of forty retired pilots, took a car to the residence of Xu Jixiang, the Director of the Marine Affairs Department of the Navy, Principal of the Pilot Training School, and Executive Committee Member of the Pilot Management Committee, to seek his assistance. Learning that Xu was in Beijing on official business, his wife met with the group and accepted their petition to pass it on to Xu. The content of the petition can be summarized into three points: 1. The previous examination was very corrupt, so they requested a re-examination. 2. The level of the previous examination was too inconsistent and lacked standards. The scope of the re-examination must be clearly defined. 3. Sufficient preparation must be allowed for the re-examination, requesting three months. During this preparation period, they should still be allowed to operate under licenses issued by the Navy to maintain their livelihood. In order to inform colleagues of the situation and promote mutual assistance, the association hosted a banquet for various maritime groups at the Guyixuan Hunan and Sichuan Restaurant on Sanma Road at 6:00 PM last night. Attendees included representatives from the Nanjun'an, Yan Ying General Society, Shipping Guild, Navigation Association, Helmsman Carpenter Mutual Aid Society, and the Drivers Association, totaling over thirty people. The chairman, Zhang Zichong, reported on the association's history since its establishment and its current position, hoping for unanimous support from the maritime groups. The representatives present all expressed their acceptance. The meeting adjourned at around 9:00 PM. It was also reported that the Shanghai Shipping Guild held a meeting at 3:00 PM yesterday. Chairman Yu Qiaqing stated that although the pilotage fees had been reduced by the customs, the amount was still difficult to accept. It was resolved that shipowners could only accept an increase in pilotage fees up to 30% of the old rate, and any amount exceeding that would not be accepted. It was also reported that the Pilot Management Committee also convened a committee meeting yesterday, but it was adjourned due to a lack of quorum.

Huarong Wood Guilty of Obstructing Commerce and Industry 176

Sentenced to Two Months' Imprisonment, Suspended for Two Years

The Huarong Coal Store, located at No. 179 Rue Poinsett in the French Concession and owned by Huarong Wood, had a relatively thriving business. It sold Chinese coal balls from the China Coal Ball Factory on North Sichuan Road. However, starting on June 1st of this year, it suddenly stopped doing business with the China Factory. Subsequently, Qiu Guozhen, an employee of the China Factory, discovered that Huarong had forged the China Factory's red label and purchased discarded trademark papers, selling inferior coal balls under the guise of Chinese coal balls for profit. The French Police received a report and Detective Lu Changsheng went to the Huarong store, seized the forged red label and arrested Huarong Wood and sent to the Second Special District Court. The Police lawyer filed a charge for obstructing agriculture, industry, and commerce. The trial has been reported previously. Yesterday, Judge Wu Fanglian questioned Huarong Wood at the Criminal Eighth Court and announced the verdict in court: Huarong Wood, with the intent to profit and deceive others, instigated the counterfeiting of a registered trademark and was sentenced to two months' imprisonment, suspended for two years. During the appeal period, he must post a 500-yuan bond and await further instructions.

Wing On Bank's Business Is Prosperous 185

The task of banks in the economic field is to develop enterprises and regulate finance, so their mission is extremely important and their scope is very wide. There have been many such organizations in Shanghai in recent years, but the Wing On Bank can be considered a rising star. This newspaper has previously reported on its social spirit. Now, the bank has informed us of its latest facilities, which not only benefit the public but also make its business prosperous, showing a rapid growth. Let us describe them separately.

International Trade Department The bank's opening declaration stated that its aim is to increase exports and recover losses. Given the immaturity of domestic industry and commerce and the bankruptcy of rural areas, even reducing the cost of necessary raw material imports is tantamount to recovering a portion of the profit, which is not easy. In recent months, the bank has made every effort to establish an international trade department. Everything related to the export of goods, including customs clearance and shipment, can be handled on behalf of customers at low fees for convenience. The import of goods, such as raw materials necessary for industry and commerce, can also be handled on behalf of customers, reducing costs by 15% compared to dealing directly with foreign firms. Experts have been invited to design and open offices to promote the initiative step by step.

Personnel Trust The domestic society is becoming increasingly complex. Personnel trust, such as estate execution and property management, is still in its infancy. To address private disputes, the bank has hired many legal and accounting experts to form a legal department. All personnel matters can be handled on behalf of customers, solving their legal problems.

Remittance Hong Kong and Guangzhou have early on been connected, so remittance inflows and outflows have been massive. The bank is fast in reporting market prices and charges lower fees. Customers in the Hongkou area are constantly entrusting remittances to the bank. Recently, over one hundred and fifty Zhejiang, Anhui and Jiangsu banks have been added to facilitate transactions.

Deposits Deposits are popular because of short terms, high-interest rates, and secure protection. The bank mainly handles loans with objects as collateral, focusing on bill discounts and pledge loans. Credit loans are not accepted. Small factories will be given various facilities.

Special Business The bank is open until 12:00 AM. It has been decided that a security measure will be in place to make the transactions safe during the winter months. For every disbursement of more than one thousand yuan, an armored vehicle will be available for free escort. For deposits, there is no need to come in person. A phone call will be assigned to receive the funds. In this way, there is no security risk for the evening inflow and outflow.

Trial of Embezzlement Case Against Employees of Nanxiang Bus Company 186

Two Defendants Flatly Deny Charges

Case Adjourned for Re-examination

This case involves the Shanghai-Nanxiang bus company, where employees Zhang Hesheng and Gu Songqiao allegedly embezzled public funds under the guise of expenses for public relations with the Public Works Bureau and the Public Security Bureau. The Public Works Bureau discovered the matter and sent a letter to the Public Security Bureau requesting a thorough investigation. The Bureau then detained Zhang and Gu and sent them to the District Court. Prosecutor Xiao Pu侦查 found the allegations to be true and filed charges in the criminal court, alleging that the defendants Zhang Hesheng and Gu Songqiao committed embezzlement. The charges stated that Zhang Hesheng was the chief of transportation for the Nanxiang Bus Company and, along with Gu Songqiao, was responsible for handling financial matters. In July of this year, they jointly embezzled over two hundred and ten yuan. Zhang Hesheng instructed the bookkeeper Wu Ciyin to record the amount as expenses paid to the Public Works Bureau and Public Security Bureau for public relations. This was discovered by the Public Works Bureau, which then handed the case over to the Public Security Bureau. The defendants were jointly responsible for managing finances at the Nanxiang Bus Company. The ledger showed payments to the Public Works Bureau and Public Security Bureau for public relations expenses, but Zhang Hesheng denied making these payments. Therefore, the sum was undoubtedly embezzled by Zhang Hesheng and Gu Songqiao. Zhang Hesheng's claim that Wu Ciyin maliciously recorded the expenses to frame him was clearly a fabrication. The defendants were accomplices in violating Article 357, Section 1 of the Criminal Code and should be prosecuted under Article 253, Section 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, requesting a public trial. Yesterday morning, Judge Sun Ji of the Fifth Tribunal specially opened a court session and ordered the defendants Zhang Hesheng and Gu Songqiao, who were in custody, to be brought before the court. Zhang Hesheng testified that he was 42 years old, from Jiading, residing at 51 Xiaoshadu Road, and currently the chief of transportation for the Shanghai Nanxiang Bus Company. Question: "Are you in charge of the finances?" Answer: "No." Question: "What are you in charge of?" Answer: "Repairing machinery and purchasing materials." Question: "Did you give 50 yuan to the Public Works Bureau on June 30th?" Answer: "That's a mistake in the ledger." Question: "What did you use the 180 yuan from July 14th and July 21st for?" Answer: "30 yuan was paid to the City Bank for licensing fees, and the rest was used to purchase parts and materials for the buses, all of which have invoices to prove it." Question: "You didn't give any of this money to the Public Works Bureau or the Public Security Bureau?" Answer: "No." Question: "Then isn't that embezzlement?" Answer: "That's a false accusation!" Question: "Can you write?" Answer: "I haven't studied." Next, Gu Songqiao testified that he was 50 years old, from Jiading. Question: "What are you in charge of?" Answer: "I manage the finances at the Shanghai branch, but I don't handle the Nanxiang branch." Question: "Who gave the money to Zhang Hesheng?" Answer: "The manager." Question: "What is Wu Ciyin's position?" Answer: "Chief Accountant." Question: "Did you pay Zhang Hesheng on June 30th?" Answer: "No, it was paid from the Nanxiang branch." Question: "What did Zhang Hesheng use the money for?" Answer: "To purchase parts." Question: "Why does the ledger say 'public relations expenses'?" Answer: "I don't know." Question: "Did you lobby for licenses with money?" Answer: "No, there was no such thing." Then, Gao Zhongyu testified that he was 38 years old, from Gaoyou, formerly an aide to the National Government's adjutant's office, and currently the chairman of the board of directors of the bus company. Question: "What is Zhang Hesheng's position?" Answer: "Chief of Transportation." Question: "Does he manage the finances?" Answer: "Yes, he does. On September 7th, Zhang came to my office by bus and said that if we wanted to operate, we had to lobby the Public Works Bureau first. That's how I knew he was misusing public funds." Question: "But Zhang Hesheng has consistently denied it." Answer: "It's recorded in the ledger, and he personally told me about it." Question: "Do you have evidence of him giving this money to someone at the Public Works Bureau?" Answer: "No evidence." The judge then ordered manager Ni, 23 years old, from Shanghai, residing in Caojiadu, to appear in court. Question: "Who is in charge of management?" Answer: "They all manage it together." Question: "Is there a rough draft of the ledger?" Answer: "Yes." Question: "Did Zhang Hesheng take this money for public relations expenses?" Answer: "Yes." Question: "Where is the rough draft of the ledger?" Answer: "At the Nanxiang branch." Finally, Wu Ciyin testified that he was 36 years old. Question: "Are you in charge of the ledger?" Answer: "Yes." Question: "Who manages the finances?" Answer: "Zhang and the other two." Question: "Who instructed you to record this payment?" Answer: "Zhang Hesheng told me to write it down." Question: "Was this record copied from the rough draft?" Answer: "No." The judge concluded that the case was complex and required further testimony. The two defendants were remanded in custody to await further hearings at a later date.

Spring and Autumn

Little West Heaven 189

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: The Imperial Decree Smiles with Fawning, the Lamp Illuminates the Wasted Face; the Intestines and Spleen are Pressed to Apply Powder and Learn Fashion

The clothes he wore, although made of silk, were made of the kind of soft satin that was excessively cheap in Jiangnan, selling for only two or three mao per foot. These clothes were still made in Jiangnan. Just looking at the length, they were not the kind that dragged behind the heels. The slits were more than a foot long, passing the knees, and the cuffs were level with the elbows. This was not the style of 1934. This proved that even if he came from Jiangnan, he had left Jiangnan for more than a year. The leather shoes he wore were no longer the latest shallow round-toe style, and a leather strap was fastened across the instep. This made him look especially old. But only Zhang Jiefu and Li Shilian could tell that he was not fashionable. In Hu Saozi's eyes, she thought he was excessively ostentatious. So she gently asked a waiter who had not left, "Is he from the Kaiyuan Temple?" (Note: Kaiyuan Temple is an ancient temple built in the Tang Dynasty and is one of the historical sites of Xi'an. Now, prostitutes live on both sides of the entrance to the temple.) The waiter glanced at the outside, frowned, and said, "I don't recognize him." As he spoke, the three men and one woman all went into Li Shilian's room. Hu Saozi stood up, clapped her hands, raised her hands, and laughed, "No need to mention it today, I'll come again tomorrow morning." As she spoke, she walked out, only to hear Li Shilian calling out, "Quick, invite Mr. Jia! Quick, invite Mr. Jia!" Although Hu Saozi had no relationship with Jia Duocai, she saw someone who looked like he was from the Kaiyuan Temple here, and now they were inviting Mr. Jia. She felt this was a bit unfair and wanted to see what was going on, so she stopped walking away and stood by the courtyard gate, leaning on the door and stretching her head inside. That was how she stood there. In less than ten minutes, hurried footsteps came, and someone laughed beside her, "You've come too?" As the person spoke, he walked past, still with a smile. Hu Saozi saw that it was Jia Duocai. (71)

Fragments of Mr. Shi Liangcai's Philosophy of Life 190

— Tian Sheweng

This was about three years ago. I was teaching in a mansion, and I had been there for a full eight years. Because those who were poisoned by [literary poison] lacked the knowledge to deal with the world, in these eight years, besides teaching, I only knew how to read, write essays, and write some ugly little pieces, submitting them to this newspaper. I had been doing this for twenty years. I didn't know how to socialize, I only knew how to be elegant. Later, because the two young masters of this mansion—who were my students—had both married and had children and were in their twenties, the head of the household treated me very kindly and gave me a year's vacation, saying, "Next year, the two young masters will go to the bank to do business and will no longer study. Please find another job." At the end of the year, of course, I had to leave with my brush pot. Because I didn't usually socialize and lacked the knowledge to deal with the world, I naturally had problems with finding a job next year.

In this mansion for eight years, because the head of the household liked to practice meditation and sitting, he was a Taoist believer. So I got to read some Taoist books. Over time, I discovered many scientific values in Taoism that even the Japanese may not have mentioned. Various books about Taoism published in bookstores did not mention this at all. I often thought of making a clear and rational explanation of my insights in a [Scientific View of Taoism] to save the ills of Western material civilization. Regarding the philosophy of life and political philosophy, I would use Taoist learning to inject healing needles. But, to this day, not a single word has been written.

With the motive of finding a job, I first turned the doctrines of Lao Zhuang into a five-thousand-word novel entitled [A Dream of Longevity], with Wei Boyang, Zhong Liquan, Lü Chunyang, Ge Xianweng, Zhang Sanfeng, and He Xiangu as characters who explained the true meaning of longevity and the philosophy of life. I also wrote a cover letter and this novel and sent them to Mr. Shi Liangcai, the general manager of this newspaper. Later, he sent a resume form and told me to fill it out and send it back. His original letter said: [Now that the country is so poor and weak, we should work hard for the country and society. Where can we sit quietly and cultivate ourselves, seeking the art of longevity alone!] - That's the general idea! From these few words, you can know Mr. Shi's philosophy of life.

Mr. Shi unfortunately encountered a disaster on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road and died in his prime, forcing me to believe in Lao Tzu's philosophy of life! But, although Lincoln is dead, his spirit lives on. We don't need to be sad for Mr. Shi.

Snippets 191

— (Jin Xiongwu)

There are many extremely common names in the world that are difficult to explain. Let's take one example. Why is the area above the lips called the "philtrum"? If we say it is the middle of the human body, it should be between the navel and abdomen. Because from here upwards, the forehead, ears, and nose are all double orifices, and from here downwards, the mouth and the two excretory openings are all single orifices. Three books of yin and three books of yang. Is this taken from the meaning of the Tai hexagram?

Imperial Fragrance Floating Record 192

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

I don't know why, but as soon as I saw the light from these corner lamps, I felt something was different; mostly because they were too dim. Looking elsewhere, in every palace and under every long corridor, the same kind of horn lanterns were hung, emitting a deep yellow light. The whole thing looked very peculiar and made me feel uneasy. It would make one have a terrifying feeling. And the entire palace of Shengjing was shrouded in this terrible light every evening! I don't admit that I am a timid person, but seeing this dim and gloomy scene made me uncontrollably have a frivolous fantasy: I thought that the people who had died in these palaces for hundreds of years were about to climb up one by one like ghosts in deep mountains and valleys. I seemed to have seen many strangely shaped black shadows shaking in front of me, causing me to tremble uncontrollably. I suspected that this unstable feeling of mine was a sign of some misfortune tomorrow.

In the main hall where the Empress Dowager lived, although the same candles were used and the same horn lanterns were used, these lanterns were not hanging above, but were installed on a dozen lamp stands. The style of these lamp stands was very special. The raw material was red sandalwood, and there were many patterns on it, but they were different from the ordinary. Although it was also completely surrounded by coiled dragons, they were neither inlaid with gold or silver nor painted with various bright paints, but were directly carved on the wood with knives, so their color was the same as the lamp stand itself, which was black. It didn't look very prominent. If you wanted to appreciate it carefully, you had to bring your eyes close to see it clearly. It was best to touch it with your fingers so that you could especially recognize the workmanship and refinement of these carvings. (181)

The Landlord's Family 193

— Wei Jing

I recently moved to Huxi and rented three Shanghai-style [local houses] on a road built across the boundary. The front faced the concession's road, and the houses were located on the Chinese territory. Behind the houses was a large open space, which the landlord used to grow vegetables.

Speaking of our landlord, he is quite interesting. The landlord is an old man of nearly fifty. It is said that he has more than ten mu of ancestral land in the Huxi area, each mu worth an average of more than 10,000 yuan, so the ten mu of land are worth about 200,000 yuan. These lands are all rented out to people, and the annual rent income is more than 10,000 yuan. But the old man wears a black cotton-padded coat and trousers, cloth socks, and cloth-soled shoes, and smokes yellow tobacco costing more than 100 cash a day. Watering, weeding, and harvesting in the vegetable garden and then carrying them to the market to sell are his only jobs.

His wife and his eldest granddaughter spend their time making long ingots and matchboxes every day, in addition to cooking and washing clothes. It is said that they can earn 200 cash a day. His son is a clerk in a foreign company. Although he will have an inheritance worth 200,000 yuan in the future, he has to walk ten miles from his home to the foreign company, regardless of wind, rain, cold, or heat. His daughter-in-law is the mother of seven children, and she does everything herself, from breastfeeding to dressing the children. His eldest grandson and second grandson each studied for three or four years and are now apprentices. They are all apprentices in foreign companies.

I moved from the bustling city to the quiet Huxi and live next to such a family. I almost suspect that I am no longer living in this city.

— Yin Juan

Glimpses of Tiger Hill (Continued) 194

— Huoxue Ming

The "Distant Fields in Level Woods" among the Twelve Scenes of Tiger Hill probably refers to this place. To the east of the pavilion, there is also a lookout, where soldiers are stationed. Presumably, from their high vantage point, the sand birds and sails on Taihu Lake, and the inch-sized horses and bean-like people in Suzhou city, cannot escape their gazing eyes.

Circling the short white-powdered wall and passing through the doorway inscribed with "Majestic," that precarious pagoda, resembling a drunken old man, stands quietly in the sunset, its bricks eroded with ancient red, revealing gray-white bones. The mud is covered with weeds from the previous dynasty, and wild birds build nests there, which cannot help but make people linger and sigh. However, the beauty of Tiger Hill Pagoda lies precisely in its incompleteness and tilting. Five years ago, when I came here to pay my respects, I fully expected that this pagoda would soon collapse. Yet today, it still adorns the Seven-Mile Shantang. Although I am still young, I fear I will not have the good fortune to witness the collapse of Tiger Hill Pagoda.

A bit melancholic along the way, I sought out the back door of Xiao Wu Xuan from among the desolate hills and rubble, only to find it guarded by soldiers. I had no choice but to pass through the Chan Temple, following the stone steps of the Fifty-Three Visits, and before my eyes was a blood-red, thousand-person stone, smooth and polished to a lovable degree. Truly, besides Tiger Hill, this piece of stone cannot be found anywhere else. As for the Nodding Stone of myth, the Broken Beam Hall, and the Sword Pond, I find them unremarkable. Especially the Tomb of Zhen Niang and the Tomb of Mandarin Ducks, they hold no meaning to chew on!

Crows fly in the sunset of the crumbling pagoda, and tourists gradually disperse. Only after the light has completely faded do I return to the gate. (The End)

Miscellaneous Remarks

Early Winter Exhibition 195

— Zhu Hui

The bright maple leaves, redder than February flowers, and the yellow blossoms under the fence, also compete in five colors, as if the earth is covered in a layer of brocade. Several refined and elegant men have even put on an exhibition to present their treasured horticultural specimens. During these past two weeks, Suzhou has held grand events at the Dongwu and Liuyuan Parks. Now, I will roughly describe some of the exhibits, to provide an on-paper appreciation for those who love horticulture.

Chrysanthemums

The varieties of chrysanthemums are truly numerous, and the colors and forms of the flowers are splendid and beautiful, each extremely exquisite. The varieties of chrysanthemums can be roughly divided into ten types: silk, ribbon, horn, petal, tube, claw, hair, ball, ruyi, and mixed color. The "silk" chrysanthemum has petals that droop like tassels, possessing a scattered and unrestrained charm; varieties like "Ten-Foot Pearl Curtain," "White Dragon Whiskers," and "Disordered Clouds" belong to this category. The "ribbon" chrysanthemum has petals that are shorter and wider than silk, spreading out boldly and exuding a refined and elegant beauty; there are varieties like White Jade Ribbon and Qilin Ribbon. The tip of the petal has a distinct corner, which is the "horn" chrysanthemum; varieties like Qilin Horn and Great Azure Dragon possess a magnificent posture. The "petal" chrysanthemum, in terms of its bearing, is too full of rich and noble air, lacking the hidden and reclusive charm. However, the large flower heads and broad petals have a kind of dignified and luxurious aura. This type of flower includes "Eighteen Petal Lotus," "Sprinkled Gold Eighteen Petal," "Green Peony," and "Snow Azure Lotus." The "tube" flower has hollow petals like tubes. Among the fine chrysanthemums, this variety is not particularly wonderful. Varieties like "Laojun Eyebrow" are very difficult to cultivate. Among the forms of chrysanthemums, the most flying, dancing, and majestic are undoubtedly the "claw" chrysanthemums. The petals of the claw chrysanthemum spread out like claws. This type of chrysanthemum generally has large flower heads and a majestic posture. Varieties include "White Dragon Claw" and "Bearded Dragon." The "hair" chrysanthemum has fine hairs growing on its petals, and includes the Yellow Hair and Green Hair varieties, which are also very beautiful in form. The "ball" flower has petals that are evenly curved and clustered together, forming a shape like a ball, which is very endearing. The "ruyi" chrysanthemum has long branches, but the flowers are small and exquisite, resembling a long-handled ruyi scepter. "Mixed color" chrysanthemums have two colors on one flower, such as "Green Robe and Red Skirt," which is light green on the outside but scarlet on the inside. "Er Qiao" has a mix of red and white, which is strangely beautiful. In addition, there are artificial tie-dyed flowers. The large ones are over a hug in circumference and almost as tall as a person, but they are too vulgar and inevitably lose the reclusive flavor of chrysanthemums.

Goldfish

In addition to the "Dragon," "Egg," and "Grass" varieties of goldfish, there are also "Pearl Fish" and "Swallowtail Fish." The scales of the pearl fish are raised one by one, round like grains of pearls; this type of goldfish is very difficult to raise. At this park's fish and chrysanthemum exhibition, the pearl fish from the Sun residence of Sijing Lane were displayed on two tables. The larger ones were nearly a foot long, which is certainly no easy feat. Although the swallowtail fish have single tails, they are particularly long and large. When swimming, they are graceful and supple, with a leisurely attitude. The violet fish are the beloved goldfish of the Violet Orchid owner, with purple spots all over their bodies. Swimming among the green algae, they have a unique and magnificent appearance. The "piled jade" fish have soft flesh piled on their heads, like a tiger's head. The "pom-pom" fish have round fleshy balls growing on either side of their mouths. They come in two varieties: loose and tight, and the large ones are the size of longans. In addition, there are "turned gills" and "bubble eyes." The gills of the "turned gill" fish are completely turned outward. The eyeballs of the "bubble eye" fish are like two soft bubbles of water. When swimming in the water, the two eyeballs can expand and contract softly. It is said that if one is not careful, they will break the bubbles and become blind fish. In addition, there is a type called "red hat," whose entire body is silver and whose head is red, as if wearing a red hat; the color is particularly bright.

Melons and Fruits

In addition to goldfish and chrysanthemums, winter melons and pearl melons are also exhibits these days. The color of the winter melon is so vermilion and fresh; the pearl melon is a variant of the winter melon. The forms vary in size, and the colors vary in yellow and white. On the outside of the melon, there are small round pearls. Matched with various porcelain pots, they are also pleasing to the eye. In this autumn wind and when ducks and crabs are fat, holding wine while admiring chrysanthemums and judging fish is indeed a pleasure in life. "Life is for pleasure." Why seek fame and fortune and bring trouble upon oneself in this world?

Education News

Shandong Qilu University Uproar Situation 207

Students Petition the Board of Directors to Demand a Formal President

Currently in a State of Idleness, Difficult to Resolve Immediately

(Nanjing, 22nd Dispatch) Student representatives from Qilu University today visited Li Zhifan, the vice-chairman of the school's board, and important figures in the provincial government, requesting assistance in resolving the president issue to avoid affecting the students' future. Li Xingxi, a member of the board, negotiated to convene a full board meeting and requested the reinstatement of President Lin Jiqing, but was refused. Li also resigned, and the uproar is expanding, with a pessimistic outlook.

[Jinan Letter] Shandong Qilu University suddenly experienced a student movement today (the 20th). Although it doesn't appear to be particularly serious, considering the school's past reputation, students would not rashly initiate such action unless absolutely necessary. It is rumored that this is solely due to the president issue. Since Acting President Lin left the school last semester, there has been no one in charge. The student roster after the summer break should normally be submitted to the province for referral to the Ministry for record-keeping, but due to the absence of a formal president, the Education Department cannot forward it and has repeatedly extended the deadline, which is now imminent. For the sake of their future and studies, the students felt compelled to unite and express themselves. Therefore, at 9:30 AM today (the 20th), they gathered in front of Zhiguo Building on campus to make a peaceful request to the board of directors. The issue remained unresolved until 3:00 PM. When the reporter arrived, Li Zhifan (the vice-chairman of the school's board) was addressing the students. According to the Student Union, this is by no means a personal issue, but rather a demand for someone to be responsible as president. The students' actions are not comparable to typical disturbances, and they are not supporting any particular faction. They simply seek mutual understanding among all parties so that the school can be officially registered. As of the time of this dispatch, it is reported that Li Zhifan has gone to Qitaiguan. Given this situation, without concrete measures, it is feared that a resolution will be difficult to achieve in the short term.

General Situation of Qilu University: Shandong Qilu University was founded long ago, thirty to forty years before the establishment of the Republic of China, originating from the Wenhuitang in Dengzhou. Seven years before the establishment of the Republic, it merged with the Guangde Academy in Qingzhou and moved to Weixian, renaming itself Guangwen Academy, which was the predecessor of the College of Arts and Sciences. The School of Medicine was formed by merging the medical school run by Dr. Nie of the American Presbyterian Church in Jinan, the medical school of the Baptist Church in Qingzhou, funding from the Beijing Union Medical College, and students, as well as the medical department of Jinling University and the Datong Hospital in Hankou. In the sixth year of the Republic of China, the Theological Seminary and Guangwen Academy in Qingzhou both moved to Jinan, thus combining the four colleges of Arts, Sciences, Medicine, and Theology to form Qilu University. In the twelfth year, the North China Union Women's Medical School was also merged into the school's medical department. In the eighteenth year, according to an order from the Ministry of Education, the Department of Theology was separated. At the end of the twentieth year, the Ministry of Education approved its registration as a private university. Currently, funding is provided by the United Church Board for World Ministries of the United Kingdom and the United States, the Luo Shi Foundation, and various departments of the Chinese government. The board of directors includes Chinese directors Li Zhifan, Yi Zhenqing, Tan Shukui, etc., and Westerners Aibadi, Sikaoti, William, etc. Kong Xiangxi is the chairman of the board. However, recently, the position of president has been vacant for a long time, and no one is formally responsible for school affairs. The student roster after the summer break could not be submitted to the Ministry for record-keeping as usual because there was no official presidential seal. Therefore, there have been some joint actions to make demands to the board of directors.

Causes of the Dispute: Since President Zhu Jingnong left Qilu University, Lin Jiqing, the dean of the College of Arts and Sciences, has been serving as acting president for two years and has achieved considerable success. On June 15th of this year, a board meeting was held, but only a few people attended to discuss the issue of the president. However, the board members could not reach a consensus. Acting President Lin decided to resign. The majority advocated for retaining Lin to continue maintaining the situation. Provincial Chairman Han Fuju, Education Director He Siyuan, Construction Director Zhang Honglie, and Finance Director Wang Gerong also telegraphed Kong Xiangxi, stating their intentions. On August 15th, another board meeting was held, with all directors in attendance, and Minister Ye also telegraphed Jinan. At that time, it was passed that Lin Jiqing would be the formal president immediately. Lin initially agreed to consider it, but it was rumored that after the start of the semester, some members of the board did not express sympathy towards him. Therefore, Lin went to Shanghai to take care of matters at the Central Bank, and Kong felt that the internal situation was complex, so he also decided to resign from the position of chairman. Around October, it was heard that the Standing Board of Directors had resolved to invite Minister Ye to become chairman and invited President Lin back to the school. De Weisi and Yi Zhenqing went to Shanghai to urge him. At that time, Lin's intention was to follow Kong's will to be chairman, while Minister Ye's intention was that if Lin returned to the school, he could take on the position of chairman. After De Weisi and others returned to Shandong, Minister Kong intended to ask the board of directors to nominate two people to go to Beijing, where Kong would personally explain and resolve internal differences. However, the Western board members firmly refused to go and recently convened a meeting of a few board members to overturn the resolutions of several previous meetings and appoint another acting president, failing to follow the resolutions of the full board meeting, abandoning the proper path. The position of acting president is indeed extremely difficult to fill, and after the summer break, numerous matters await the handling of a formal president. This is why the students are urgently demanding a resolution.

Recent Situation: Qilu University students have historically had strengths and weaknesses. Their strength lies in their focus on studies and their disinterest in external affairs. However, at times, large-scale groups are not easily united. This time, their joint demand for the board of directors to promptly appoint a president shows that their emotions have reached an extreme and tense state. Without a formal president, the student roster cannot be submitted to the province for referral to the Ministry, which is disturbing to the students. This is not a disturbance or a strike but only a minimal request to the board of directors, a formal and peaceful expression. Yesterday (the 20th) at 9:30 AM, male and female students gathered in the dormitories and went to the school's office building. At that time, while the board of directors was in session, representatives from the Student Union Congress and the Student Union Executive Committee submitted a petition. When they were received, only four members of the board of directors were present, which did not meet the legal quorum, and all were Westerners. At that time, the students questioned that the school had been without a president for more than a day. At the last full board meeting (August 15th), it was resolved to retain Minister Kong Xiangxi as chairman and to retain Lin Jiqing as president. Since the dispatch of representatives was resolved by the board of directors, why did this meeting overturn the opinions of the majority with a few people? Second, the representatives went to Beijing and Shanghai to retain Kong and Lin, respectively, and Kong and Lin both had intentions to act. Why did the board of directors ignore this, resulting in the student roster not being submitted to the Ministry? This is not a fact of non-permission but an error by the board of directors. Third, they questioned how the board of directors, unwilling to sacrifice its prejudices, would resolve the students' personal roster, which could not be submitted to the Ministry. However, the board of directors did not provide a satisfactory response to this. The students agreed to stay in front of the office building, standing in the biting cold wind. Not only did the Western board members lack a definite attitude, but their imposing manner was regrettable. After a while, Li Zhifan, the vice-chairman of the school's board, arrived after hearing the news and addressed the students, stating that he had returned to Jinan this morning and that the school's problem was very complex. However, this was a matter for the board of directors itself, and the board members were discussing methods to seek a resolution. Later, he left due to other matters. By about 4:00 PM, the students had not completely dispersed, and the outcome may not be resolved in the short term.

Shanghai Art College to Hold New Campus Groundbreaking Ceremony Today 215

At 10:00 AM at the New Site on Caojing Road

With Cai Yuanpei, Sun Ke, and Others as the Presidium

The Shanghai Art College is celebrating its 23rd anniversary today (the 23rd). At 10:00 AM this morning, a groundbreaking ceremony will be held for the new campus in the South District of Shanghai on Caojing Road. At the same time, an autumn painting and writing exhibition and a music concert will be held at the school on Caishi Road to commemorate the occasion. Details are as follows:

New Campus Groundbreaking Ceremony

The site of the school's new campus is located south of Xujiahui Town and north of Caojing Town, in a quiet and tranquil area free from the hustle and bustle of the city. It is conveniently located on the Shanghai-Hangzhou National Highway. The groundbreaking ceremony will be held at the site at 10:00 AM on the 23rd. The presidium will consist of Cai Yuanpei, Sun Ke, Wu Tiecheng, Ye Gongchuo, Du Yong, Qian Yongming, Wang Jiyuan, the school's board of directors, members of the construction committee, leaders of fundraising teams, alumni, students, and faculty. The route to the site is from Xujiahui, past Jinji Bridge, turning onto Xietu Road, heading west directly to Caojing Road. The reception will be located in the Cao Garden.

New Building Planning

The school organized a construction committee in the spring of last year to plan the construction of the new campus and art gallery, inviting forty capable people to serve as fundraising team leaders. Currently, the teams have collected more than 10,000 yuan in donations, and uncollected pledges are being pursued. The school's main buildings include practical and theoretical classrooms, dormitories for male and female students, an office, an auditorium, an art gallery, a library, an animal house, a botanical garden, and a sports field. The entire building will be constructed in three phases, starting with the main part, which will be contracted to the Shanghai Dachang Construction Company and will begin construction next month. The second phase of construction will begin upon completion of the building, and the entire project will be completed by the autumn of next year.

Exhibition and Concert

The school holds a landscape painting exhibition after each semester's sketching trip. To celebrate the 23rd anniversary of the school, it has been expanded and renamed the Autumn Painting and Writing Exhibition. In addition to displaying all the works from the sketching trips, it will also display Chinese paintings of landscapes, flowers, and birds, as well as figures, watercolors, and charcoal drawings of Western paintings. It will be held at the school on Caishi Road, starting on the 23rd. A music concert will be held in the school's Yi Hai Tang at 7:00 PM on the 24th to celebrate the anniversary. Guests are admitted by invitation, and a grand occasion is expected.
