Free Talk

Artistic Products 216

— Zhou Muzhai

In ancient times, critiques of art and literature, poetry, prose, painting, and even calligraphy, were often called something "product," something "product." In terms of poetry, the most famous is Zhong Rong's "Poetry Products," which divided one hundred and three poets from the Han and Wei dynasties to the Liang dynasty into three grades. There is also Sima Kongtu's "Poetry Products," which is divided into more, with twenty-four grades.

The original meaning of the word "product" is numerous. "Shuowen": "Product, the common people, from three mouths." Duan Yucai's note: "Three people are numerous, so from three mouths, associative." The nature of the word "product" is descriptive. Yi Yun: "Products flow and take shape." The extended meaning, as a noun, includes rank, objects, and style; as a verb, it includes evaluation. Although the word "product" used to critique art and literature also has the meanings of objects and style, it mainly refers to rank. This rank is a reflection of the hierarchical system of feudal society.

If the critique is called "product" and the conclusion of the critique is also called something "product," has the original meaning of the word "product" been lost? It is still there in essence. Feudal society is a society of ranks, and the ranks of feudal society are numerous. When numerous ranks are reflected in art and literature, ranks are also numerous. This is one explanation. Criticisms differ from person to person. The ranks of art and literature also differ from person to person. This is called "three people are numerous, so from three mouths." This is another explanation.

Now, the main meaning of the word "product" is object. All manufactured goods are called "products," and art and literature are no exception. All manufactured goods are commodities, and art and literature are still rarely an exception. "Store it in famous mountains, pass it on to its people." The transmission between teachers and disciples in this patriarchal society is already a thing of the past. "Inspiration cannot be sold, but that article can be sold." This common saying quoted in the book "Art and Criticism" is only half right. Because articles can be sold, the inspiration entrusted to them can also be sold. From this perspective, I doubt the words "nature and spirit." Are the "nature and spirit works" of those who flaunt "nature and spirit"—here, the word "product" must be avoided—sold or not? If they are sold, "nature and spirit" also become trademarks.

Some people ask why there are no great creations, and some people scold essays, believing that the absence of great creations is due to the prevalence of essays. The meaning of the absence of great creations is not that there are no creations, but that those that exist are not necessarily great. If this is true, even though they are creations, they are no different from essays. The difference between creation and essays is only a change of form in writing. This is why everyone is writing essays, which are ungreat creations. This can be viewed in the same way as the fate of Chinese industry. The products are of poor quality and small scale.

Because their own industrial products are not good, there is both the popularity of foreign goods and the promotion of domestic goods. In art and literature, there are both people engaged in creation and people engaged in translation. However, this cannot be viewed in the same way. Industry is constrained by foreign countries, but the facts are clear: should we promote domestic goods, improve domestic goods, and adopt Western methods, or should we continue to use local methods?

Artistic products have been determined to be commodities. Of course, we should not regard them as sacred just because they are not like this, but we do not need to think that this is an insult. Commodities cannot be treated as the same. They include luxury goods manufactured for special people, vulgar crude products, and products that are in between.

Catching "[Rats]" 217

— Dangtian

Recently, I came from the north and lived in a friend's house. My friend is nearsighted, and so am I.

One night, my friend came out of the bathroom and said that he saw a big rat inside, asking if I wanted to kill it. I remembered the amusing scene from my childhood of catching a rat, drenching its body with kerosene, and burning it publicly. I also recalled that when I woke up from a dream a few nights ago, I seemed to feel a rat jumping around the bed. So I jumped out of bed, put on my glasses, and said to my friend, "Yes! Yes! Let's do it right away!"

The bathroom and the pavilion room are connected, with only a board wall in between. There is no light in the bathroom, only the light from the pavilion room shines in. Our first action was to close the bathroom door tightly, for fear that the rat would escape. The second action was to start looking for weapons—things to kill the rat with. The two of us stood in the pavilion room and looked for a while, thought for a while, ran to the upper floor and stood for a while, and then went to this room to ask. Finally, my friend held a cookie jar, and I took a broken paper umbrella, pushed open the door and walked in, with him guarding the door and me using the umbrella to stir under the bathtub. Dong! A black-haired "[rat]" about a foot long and weighing more than two pounds jumped out, hit the board wall, and hid back under the bathtub. The "[rat]" was so thick and fierce that my friend was already so frightened that he threw away the jar and stepped on the edge of the bathtub. I was also taken aback, although I still held the broken umbrella tightly in my hand. After the two of us regained our composure, we were surprised to find that such a large "[rat]" was not easy to see. I was afraid that it could only be found in the trenches of the First World War, so I felt that it had to be killed. So my friend borrowed a firewood knife and two pine logs from a landlord, and I took off my slippers and put on a pair of basketball shoes, ready to stomp on it a few times. This time, my friend was still the doorkeeper, holding two pine logs in both hands, I held a broken umbrella in my left hand, and a firewood knife in my right hand. I poked the broken umbrella under the bathtub: no response, I stirred hard, but it was still the same. We suspected that the "[rat]" had escaped when we went to find weapons the second time, but the floor of the bathroom was cement, and there was definitely no hole. The two windows were tightly closed, and we didn't forget to push the door shut when we came out. The locking work was done so tightly that it was really impossible for it to escape, so we persisted and stirred frantically under the bathtub. Dong! The "[rat]" that had appeared just now jumped out again, hit the board wall, and hid under the bathtub. Pine logs, firewood knives, broken umbrellas, and basketball shoes did not show their effect.

My friend said that it was not easy to start and did not want to fight anymore; but I was not willing to give up and asked him to think of a better way together. As a result, he suggested using wooden boards to block the two sides of the bathtub that were not against the wall and pouring a bucket of boiling water down, and the "[rat]" would naturally be scalded to death; I thought there was really no better way than this, so I agreed with him. I stayed there to watch; he went outside to ask the water store to deliver water. After a while, he came back, holding a small iron bar in his hand, followed by a water delivery worker. My friend told him about our "[work]," and he immediately agreed to participate together. This time I was still responsible for searching, and the worker replaced my friend's just position, guarding the door. I still used the broken umbrella as the vanguard, inserted it under the bathtub, and stirred for a long time without seeing any sound. I struck a match to look inside, and a ball of hand-like things curled up in the corner. The worker saw that I was nearsighted and said to me, "Let me do it, give me the matches!" The matches were handed to him. He squatted down, looked at the bottom of the bathtub, struck a match, and immediately said, "Oh! A kitten!" My friend and I were both horrified, looked at each other, and I really can't analyze the mood at that time. "No way?" I woke up from the abyss of disappointment and uttered this sentence. The worker struck another match, shone it on the gap between the wall and the bathtub, poked his head in to look, and still said "A kitten, black!"

My friend laughed, and so did I. A terrible social scene unfolded in my heart. We were thankful that we were not the kitten's destroyers.

Roadside Shop (Part 1) 218

— Liu Ming

—One of the Memories of a Thousand Cliffs—

A sudden sound of rain hitting a paper umbrella started under the eaves. A bald-headed monk wrapped in a yellow kasaya walked in, loudly yelling "Aha!" Immediately, his muddy feet left a string of muddy footprints on the newly swept floor, along with droplets of water falling from the umbrella. He used a mixture of Bai Yi and Han Chinese everyday phrases, calling out to the owner of the shop [Bifa, bring me a pack of cigarettes!] Then he leaned the wet umbrella against the foot of the bed and plopped down on the bed where the opium lamp was placed. Being stranded in this thatched hut under the Yellow Fruit Tree, dodging the first malarial rain in the Bai Yi region, already made us feel heavy and unhappy. Now, seeing a pair of large feet covered in mud, sticking up high on the edge of the bed, glaringly in front of us, made us even more irritable and uneasy.

A sedan chair carrier, taking advantage of the rain when no one needed a ride, sat by the bamboo window, drilling small holes in a bamboo pole used for carrying people, planning to inject cooked opium, hoping to get past the wild men's patrol at the Xima River. Upon seeing the sudden arrival of the Bai Yi monk, he quickly put aside what he was doing, pretending to be nonchalant, hiding his displeasure, yet revealing it through his pursed lips, muttering a sentence [Even monks are smoking opium,] just as he saw the female owner, whom the Bai Yi monk called Bifa (sister-in-law), displaying the joy of welcoming a distinguished guest, calling him "Buddha, Buddha," trying her best to be gentle and flattering to please him, which made him mutter another indistinct curse.

[Tch, look at that! Humph, old and indecent!]

People from the lower class always love to express their emotions without restraint, which often leads to fights. If a fight broke out in this small roadside shop, it would make it even more unbearable to stay. So, I adopted a calming attitude and patted him on the shoulder.

[Hey, keep your voice down, the owner's son might hear you!]

Immediately, two other people, his partner and a private opium seller who yawned all day long, couldn't help but burst into laughter. At the same time, I noticed the female owner's son, turning his rough, thirty-year-old face from his shoulder, showing an embarrassed expression, quickly turning back, still sitting by the earthen stove with his head lowered, guarding the vigorously bubbling opium pot. Perhaps because they saw his embarrassment, the three of us laughed even harder, a short dry tobacco pipe trembling in his hand, actually falling to the ground.

[Laughing your mouth off, how will you be able to pee in sheets?]

The female owner ran over, grabbed one person's ear with one hand, pulled it hard, and cursed viciously. Then she turned around, grabbed the umbrella by the foot of the bed, and exclaimed:

[Oh dear, what a puddle!]

The man cooking opium didn't even bother to turn his head this time, just anxiously scratching the black turban wrapped around his head, while Jin Bi's small ladle clinked jarringly on the edge of the copper pot holding the opium.

[As if he's only fifteen! Hehe.]

On the Translation of [Don Quixote] 219

— Tang Xiru

The call for a Chinese translation of Don Quixote in Free Talk, if I remember correctly, has already been mentioned twice, including Mr. Miao Lie's [The Translation We Need] on November 15th.

Is there really no fool in China willing to do such a [niche] thing? No, there is. I've seen it with my own eyes. However, he was not fortunate enough to be favored by publishers, so he was not fortunate enough to be known to the public. I think this is probably because the translator is an [unknown person]? This pain, this sorrow, should be shared by many [anonymous] writers and translators.

I still remember the late autumn two years ago. I was unemployed in Guangzhou. Because I was too bored and because I lived on Fangcao Back Street, right across from the back gate of Zhongshan University, I went to the library every day to translate French writer Maurois' biography of Byron. At the same time, there was a thin, slightly dark-skinned young man with thick glasses, who looked like a [impractical] fool, who also came early and returned late, sometimes still sitting in the library at night. He was also tirelessly translating a book. Later, because we ran into each other more often, sometimes because we both fought over a dictionary or encyclopedia, we simply sat together. In those shared moments, I discovered that this foolish gentleman was translating an amazing work, namely Cervantes' Don Quixote.

When I saw him translating this book, I heard that he had been translating it for more than two years, twelve or thirteen hours a day. He had nearly finished translating two volumes of the original text, but he still needed about a year to do the annotations.

His translation style was faithful, at least his attitude was very faithful. I saw him referring to Italian translations, French translations, (he was working from the English translation) I saw him flipping through English dictionaries, French dictionaries, Japanese dictionaries, Spanish dictionaries. I also saw him asking many foreign professors at Zhongshan University. Sometimes I saw him translate less than a thousand words a day, and I was afraid for his [ants moving a mountain] work, fear mixed with admiration, admiring his perseverance in the face of difficulties. Finally, thinking about his ant-like speed, and that he was actually about to reach the end of this long journey, I couldn't help but be happy for him, and I admired him even more.

In the spring of the second year, I finished translating Byron's biography. At the same time, it seemed that he had also finished his annotation work. I ran into him on the street more often than in the library. I saw him sitting in a rickshaw many times, his head drooping, his face gloomy. Later, as I was about to leave Guangzhou and return to Shanghai, I once saw his face light up. Then, the next day, his translation of Don Quixote was published in the supplement of Guangzhou's Republican Daily. I then realized the origin of his gloomy face, and I also learned that his name was [Mo Wu], and that he was just a student at Zhongshan University. Whether Mo Wu is his real name or a pen name, I still have some doubts.

I dare not say that no one went to the library every day to read his translation, but I was one who did every day. I gained a deeper understanding of the faithfulness and fluency of his translation.

I came back to Shanghai, and my biography of Byron was rejected by various bookstores as expected. At the same time, I often thought about the fate of this translator, who was ten times more foolish than I was. Even his fate in the "ass" of the newspaper would probably not be smooth for long, right? Who wants to read this dull (!) and lengthy translation that is neither "[I love]" nor "[His mother's]?"

Unexpectedly, someone actually asked for a Chinese translation of Don Quixote in Free Talk. I felt a surge of infinite joy for Mr. Mo Wu, and another tremor of heartbreaking sadness.

The Cripple (2) (Written by Zsigmond Moricz) 220

— Translated by Uncle Zhuang

Now I must confess that I was staring blankly at him. This one thousand acres of land only supported three workers last winter. But what was that "half person" he just mentioned?

[Ah! Yes,] he said with a smile, [that cripple… my cripple… he was originally a villager in my family… When the rural reform measures were implemented, our landlord mainly wanted us to take in a cripple, so we could get a few extra [acres]. In this way, we could save a piece of land that would have been used to support this cripple. For me, he earned me sixty [acres]… For him, it was also a good deal, because his livelihood was solved… He only had one foot left, injured during the Great War (i.e., the World War from 1914 to 1918—Translator), and received 100% compensation from the government.]

Earning sixty [acres] from a cripple is indeed no trivial matter.

Passing in front of the cowshed, I saw a strange little mud hut. I thought it was a house for storing potatoes, corn, or wheat. But a chimney on the roof was emitting smoke.

[What is this?] I asked.

[This is where the cripple lives,] the landlord said, [the place where the cripple lives.]

[Can I go in?]

[Of course.]

The small hut had a door so small that one could barely enter by folding the body in half. We arrived at a tiny room that served as both a kitchen and a living room, but the largest part was occupied by the stove and a large laundry tub.

A door on the right led to a small corner. A happy little woman with a radiant face emerged from that tiny corner.

[Good day, gentlemen,] she said cheerfully.

[Good day, madam,] I said, [may we be allowed to visit your house?]

[Come in, come in,] she replied, [this is a small but lovely house…] Then she stepped aside to let us in.

The house didn't even have a small loft for storing杂物. The mud roof was finely plastered with lime. The only window was no bigger than a handkerchief worn as decoration in a coat pocket. A bed, a table, two chairs, and a small cabinet were all the furniture. In fact, that room could only fit this much.

[How many people live here?]

[My husband and I, and three children.]

[This is the only thing they know how to do,] the landlord said with [a touch of displeasure], [having children! Three in four years, not bad!]

[Ah! Sir!] the woman replied, putting her hand洁地 to her mouth where her front teeth were missing, [we've been married for five years.]

At this moment, someone came to find the landlord; a cow was giving birth. Looking worried, the landlord left, because a cow was a valuable thing.

[Please sit down,] the woman said to me, pointing to a chair.

I sat down.

Domestic Circulation of Silver Requires Permits 225

Yesterday, many were preparing to ship back through customs—

This year's large-scale export of silver has been significant, as repeatedly reported in the newspapers. After the customs authorities, acting on orders, increased the export tax, it decreased. However, in the most recent month or so, the continuous transport of silver to various locations has been incessant, and the amount is considerable. Yesterday, the Chaozhou and Guangdong Hakka merchant groups declared to a certain British shipping company that they were shipping 300 boxes of silver dollars, scheduled to be exported today. As they were in the process of clearing customs and loading the ship, the customs suddenly received an order from the Ministry of Finance stating that silver being transported to various domestic ports must have a permit from the Ministry of Finance before it could be shipped out. As a result, the customs authorities detained the silver dollar customs declarations, ordering the merchants to obtain permits, otherwise the goods would be returned. They all stopped loading. It is reported that some dozens of boxes were rerouted to Hong Kong, paying taxes there.

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the various merchants groups came to pre-order a total of about 5,000 stones of goods arriving on the 30th. The sales were like before because the market was still carrying the same attitude, the market did not change. Various Qingdao Jiutai specialized groups purchased four to five bundles. The various groups were bidding a few cents to a dime higher for rice, while the various thick japonica varieties were less attractive because the market had been usually at the same price. High-quality goods were up slightly by a few cents. The middle-grade goods were all stable. The markets for Duyang tip rice and Yinyuan rice were all stable.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of goods from He Xia on the 16th and 17th were robust in the early market, but turned sluggish in the afternoon market. The sales of Yangdubuting tip rice and thin rice were tepid. The old Baiyuan Yinyuan were more sluggish. There were some brewery customers. The market for white japonica was tight in the early market, but turned tired in the afternoon market. In the end, high-quality goods were stable, while middle- and lower-grade goods were tired and nearly a dime down. The prices for Yangdubuting tip rice, old Baiyuan Yinyuan were fair. The prices for thin rice and early rice were down a few cents.

Foreign Rice Arrives Continuously 235

Customer fragrant rice is down a dime...Foreign rice is down a dime. Yesterday's foreign rice market suddenly turned weak again. Due to the shipment of 2,500 tons of Saigon rice and 400 tons of broken rice by Atusi, totaling nearly 30,000 bags. Moreover, more than 10,000 bags of Yangtze fragrant rice also arrived. There are still two ships, including Atusi, carrying foreign rice on the way, expected to arrive soon. Even customer fragrant rice is being shipped out sporadically. In addition, there are also three or four batches of Annam japonica transported via Hong Kong. Therefore, the market sentiment became unstable. Local customers want to handle this, but stopped again. Yesterday, the market for foreign rice fell by a dime, while the customer fragrant rice fell by a dime to two dimes. Yesterday, the Zhejiang merchant group had a very weak appetite, and after a small price cut, sold 2,000 bags, and Wuxi also sold more than 2,000 bags. Total sales of customer fragrant rice were 7,300 bags, and foreign rice was more than 2,000 bags. The total transaction volume was about 10%. Foreign merchants are still seeking to sell futures rice, but the entry price is very tight, so a deal of 1,600 tons of Saigon forward cargo could not be reached.

White Sesame Sales Move Foreign Installations 236

Recently, the sales of sesame have been quite strong, due to the activity of foreign installations. Since the procurement began, there have been three or four thousand tons. The procurement is still intermittent, so the market atmosphere is still stable. Yesterday, the auction price was heard to be 7.05 yuan to 6.93 yuan. Zhangba opened at 6.90 yuan, Bengbu sesame at 6.72 yuan, Mingguang sesame at 2.20 yuan, Gaoyou sesame at 6.45 yuan, and Liuhe sesame at 6.60 yuan to 40 cents. There are still four to five thousand bags in stock, making it difficult to develop. The prices for high-quality goods opened at 6.10 yuan and 5 cents.

The report that the San Francisco Stock Exchange would auction raw silk, and Chinese silk would also be available for settlement, has been finalized. Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentaries

Banning Corrupt Titles 240

— Pi

According to the 18th Jing Bao newspaper, "[The interior ministry has recently issued an order to all provinces to ban corrupt titles such as 'Master,' 'Madam,' 'Miss,' and 'Young Master,' to avoid being ridiculed by foreign countries. It is also ordered that in the future, everyone should be referred to as 'Mr.,' 'Old Mr.,' or 'Student.']"

The telegram is brief and may lack detail. I will now extend the meaning of what was publicly stated in the telegram. The need to ban corrupt titles is of course the right thing to do. First, these titles have an exceptionally strong feudalistic color. Second, they expose a kind of class consciousness. An explicit prohibition is extremely reasonable.

However, uniformly calling everyone "Mr." or "Old Mr." still needs to be considered. It is certainly acceptable to refer to all men as "Mr.," but it is inevitably confusing to refer to women as "Mr." Although men and women are now equal, there are physiological differences between the sexes. In my opinion, married women should be called "Mrs. (女先生)," and unmarried women should be called "Ms. So-and-so (某某女士)," or simply "Miss So-and-so (某某小姐)." The word "Miss" does not have a class connotation. Words such as "Elder Sister (大姐)," "Sister (阿姐)," "Fourth Sister (四姐)," and "Third Sister (三姐)" are common terms.

Just as in foreign countries, men are called "Mr.," unmarried women are called "Miss," and married women are called "Mrs.," there is a way to indicate sex. Although our country does not necessarily need to imitate the West, it is natural that there should be a clear distinction between men and women.

As for being ridiculed by foreign countries, that may not necessarily be the case, because customs and habits are different. Foreigners find many of our country's titles and etiquette strange, and our people see many foreigners' titles and etiquette as peculiar. Taking titles as an example, calling someone "Mr." or "Mrs.," or etiquette such as men and women shaking hands when meeting, are now commonplace, but when they were first seen during the early days of trade, they were not necessarily considered strange.

However, exposing feudal colors and displaying unequal concepts are just one aspect of titles. Matters such as weddings, funerals, celebrations, and condolences have not yet had a set of common rituals, and people often follow the old ways of the Qing dynasty and embellish them, with feudal colors and class concepts displayed everywhere. These corrupt rituals should also be strictly prohibited, so that such strange phenomena will not reappear in society. These matters, along with titles, deserve attention.

The most difficult thing to abolish from the feudalistic color is the dress system. The clothes that people wear today are still following the old ways of the Qing dynasty, and it would be best to reform them. Long gowns and mandarin jackets are not considered strange because of habit, but considering the circumstances of the Qing dynasty's entry into China, it is easy to understand why changing clothes was so difficult and opposed by the people. Moreover, the long gown system is based on rules, regulations, and a measured pace, fully expressing a weak attitude. In the past, King Wuling of Zhao advocated wearing nomadic clothing to promote a martial spirit. In today's world of bloodshed, there is no place in the world for weak countries, so the clothing system should also be reformed. This is another matter.

Page 18

The Web of Life 241

— Zhang Yu

When I was little, my companions and I would catch sparrows. We would set up a net in the yard, sprinkle rice under it, and prop up one corner with a bamboo stick. A rope was tied to the top of the stick and ran into the main room. Several pairs of small eyes would watch from the bright paper window the group of small animals trapped on the roof, calling and flying back and forth, as if discussing whether to risk stealing the food in the trap below. After chirping for a while, the experienced old sparrows would surely warn them that enemies were lying in ambush below. They would tell stories, etched on their worldly wise faces, of old comrades who had lost their lives in such circumstances. The little sparrows would listen quietly, deeply believing that the stories were true, but the image of the rice grains, as alluring as a woman, would remain at the corner of their eyes. They would want to take a chance, hoping to be the lucky one to escape the terrible crisis. Of course, warning signs are never effective in the face of the sustenance of life. We use this net to lure those who risk their lives for survival.

Now, we sparrow-catching companions are ourselves hesitating in the invisible web of life. Some have already boldly stepped forward without regard for the consequences. Of course, we will never forget the sight of those little sparrows struggling in the net. When we moved to kill them, they would try to escape until their last breath while in our grasp. Seeing this cruel act, our companions would tremble and be unable to support their small bodies. Some would faint in the net before we could kill them. Now, the executioners are closing in on the trap of this net. Another type of executioner will never let us go either. So why not try to avoid this crisis? Can't we live outside the net? We have already erected these warning signs in front of everyone. We carefully avoid this web of life, hoping to be like the small sparrows on the roof, freely moving from this branch to that, or chasing each other in the open space. But the image of the rice grains, as alluring as a woman, remains at the corner of our eyes. Step by step, we approach this web of life. Unlike the small sparrows, we don't hope to be the lucky ones to escape the terrible crisis. We know that it is impossible to escape. Once we become a prisoner in this net, we are already on the execution ground. But we cannot endure the immediate coercion. The rice grains are pressuring us to be ruled by the net. In the grasp of this overwhelming authority, warning signs will never be effective!

My Wife in the Hospital 242

— Jing Yun

Thinking about my wife holding our newborn baby as she leaves the hospital, I secretly feel very happy. Because a family of just a husband and wife is indeed too lonely! Sometimes, when one side is in a bad mood or is affected by external stimuli, the two sides often quarrel over trivial matters. Moreover, my wife is a very competitive woman, and she often stubbornly refuses to compromise, causing her bright eyes to swell and turn as red as walnuts.

"Maybe having a child will be our buffer. At that time, the trivial and unreasonable quarrels between us will be reduced invisibly by the child's innocent laughter. Therefore, the family will become harmonious, I think." Whenever my wife and I argued, and we both felt a little remorseful, I would always say this to her, and she would nod silently in agreement.

Now that my wife is about to leave the hospital with our newborn baby, I secretly wish for a harmonious family: from now on, there will be no more unreasonable quarrels and disputes. But the hospital bill that I had to pay when my wife was about to be discharged made me feel very uneasy.

"Ren! The doctor already saw me this morning. He said that my fever has subsided, and if I don't have a fever again tonight, then I can be discharged..." My wife propped her back with a pillow and sat up halfway from the bed, with a smile on her lips. "I think it's okay to go out. It's not the best solution to lie here for recovery. At the same time, it can save some hospital money. Besides, you have to come here to accompany me every day, which takes up too much of your valuable time..."

"Uh, but... you still have to stay..." My throat felt as heavy as a lead block.

In fact, the doctor had already told me that my wife's fever had subsided and that she could be discharged. However, I had been running around this morning for money, and I had suffered a lot of anger and been rebuffed by many friends. They all seemed to know the purpose of my visit, and as soon as they saw me, they would first tell me how poor they were. But in order to make my wife feel at ease and not hurt her fragile heart, I had to swallow all this anger and not let it out. Although I also hoped that my wife could be discharged sooner, it was not possible to do so quickly due to financial difficulties.

"What?... Ren! Do you still want me to spend more days of loneliness and quiet in the hospital?" My wife asked, her voice louder than before, clearly with some anger.

"No, why are you angry again?" I moved my seat closer and held her trembling hand tightly. "You have to rest well and recover completely. That's very important, especially for us who have fallen on hard times! Besides, the weather is getting colder day by day, and that attic is really too narrow and cold. We have to find a better place to live."

"I think I should go out sooner, because if I stay any longer, the money will definitely be used up too much. We should consider our strength," my wife said slowly, her tone as calm and weak as an old person. I guessed that she must have remembered the terrible days of past hardship.

After a few minutes of silence, I finally broke the silence and said.

"Nong! Just bear with it and stay a day or two more before being discharged."

Although children are innocent and lovely, the thought of my wife's hospital bill filled my heart with discomfort and pain!

Shanghai Women Workers' Lives 243

First cry, second jump, third time, sit in jail. —Spinning factory folk song—

Uncle Chun 244

— A Le

My neighbor, Uncle Chun, people call him a monster. Although he is nearly sixty years old and his hair is white, his spirit is still strong. If you like to talk to him, he won't show any sign of fatigue even for a whole day. However, he only does that for people he deems worthy. Sometimes, even when someone he deems worthy talks to him, he will sit silently or stand blankly, leaving you to talk to the sky alone.

Because he is such a person, naturally few people get along with him, especially since he is also an old man.

He often walks alone in the wilderness, lingering silently under an ancient pine tree. Only when the sun sets and the birds return to the forest does he slowly stroll home. In the evening, he must drink, and he must drink until he is drunk.

At this time, if you enter his only quiet room, you must sit there silently, waiting for him to speak first. Otherwise, he will rudely throw you out.

Once, just as he had returned from the wilderness one evening, I barged into his room and sat there silently, watching him drink.

He took a sip, put down his glass, paused for a moment, then picked it up again, his eyes wide as if lost in thought, staring at the table.

Suddenly, he jumped up, slapped the table, and angrily said:

[Damn it!]

But immediately, as if he had only realized someone was in his room after saying that, he returned to his normal state and said with a faint smile:

[Drinking?]

[No.] I replied.

[Not being able to drink is a big loss.]

[I don't think so.]

He continued to smile, sat down, picked up his glass, and continued to drink.

This time, for some reason, he spoke particularly little. In the past, he would undoubtedly have expounded his grand theories or cursed heaven and earth, pouring out all his grievances with the help of alcohol. But tonight, he was unusually calm. I also felt it was too boring, so I bid him farewell and left his home.

A few days later, when I returned home from school, my younger brother told me, seemingly urgently:

[Uncle Chun is dead.]

I was stunned in surprise for a long while. My younger brother continued with difficulty:

[The day before yesterday afternoon, someone saw him sitting under that pine tree he used to like to sit under, sometimes wailing and sometimes laughing loudly. People were used to his behavior, so no one paid attention to him. Who would have thought he would die there! It is said that his corpse was still embracing that broken pine tree and wouldn't let go.]

Uncle Chun is dead. The reason why Uncle Chun hugged that pine tree before his death is still a mystery to this day.

Amateur Mailbox

An Extremely Difficult Matter 245

Editor:

I am a clerk in a shop. Recently, I have encountered many contradictory phenomena that are making me very troubled. Therefore, I am sacrificing one hour of precious sleep time to write this letter to you, hoping you can give me some guidance.

In this era of strong neighbors bullying us, most people are trying to resist and working hard for the country, resisting enemy goods, and so on. However, our manager is scheming to smuggle in enemy goods in order to make a huge profit. At the same time, if a competitor has already imported a certain enemy good that he doesn't have, he becomes very anxious, fearing that he will not be able to compete with them for profit. Even if someone calls him a traitorous merchant, he always smiles and says, [Yes, to be a merchant is to be a traitor]. In terms of conscience, with national disaster looming, one should not work for the enemy. But according to the facts, an old businessman naturally has to find ways to make profits in order to survive. I am now a clerk. [I receive my salary here, and I should be loyal here], but loyalty to the shop also goes against my conscience. How should I cope with this contradictory environment? I hope you can give me an answer. Sincerely,

Qun Sheng

Editor's note: In this era, everything is full of contradictory phenomena. Thus, young people generally feel very painful due to the surrounding contradictions and the blows from reality. The contradictory life that Mr. Qun Sheng described can be said to be representative of a portion of people.

However, the editor believes that if we can recognize the essence of contradiction, this phenomenon can instead increase our understanding of current affairs, increase our grief and anger, and increase our determination and courage to actively prepare to break the contradictions. This is overcoming contradiction, rather than being overcome by it. If you suffer from the pain of contradictory phenomena, but you don't know how to recognize it and overcome it, you will only be surrounded by pain all day long, unable to escape. You will become a prisoner of the environment, never able to free yourself!

The fact that most merchants have no national concept and smuggle in enemy goods for profit during this period of deepening national crisis is a reflection of the entire political system not being on the right track and the national spirit not being invigorated. Regarding this matter, from a small perspective, one can choose opportunities to use legitimate means to restrain these traitorous merchants at any time. But from a larger perspective, one should pay attention to the direction of the entire political and diplomatic situation and engage in the preparation of the entire nation in order to eliminate this bad phenomenon. Indignation, grief, and passive complacency are of no help to the facts.

Based on this idea, the editor believes that Mr. Qun Sheng can temporarily endure and continue to work, waiting for future opportunities. As long as he does not directly purchase and transport enemy goods, he has a clear conscience. Otherwise, he can only seek other developments; however, before finding another job, he does not need to feel too sad and angry, because we have already said that sadness and anger alone cannot compensate for the facts!

National Studies 249

Ms. Bingmei's Tang Poetry

Hua Xing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Watching Hua Sun Granddaughter Disciple Dance Sword Art

In the past, there was a beauty, Madam Gongsun

One dance with swords moved all directions

Viewers' faces were ashen and dejected

Heaven and earth were humbled for a long time

Swift as Yi shooting down nine suns

Agile as deities riding dragons to soar

Coming like thunder gathering the wrath of sunset clouds

Ceasing like rivers and seas congealing azure light

Red silk skirt and pearl sleeves, both lonely

Later disciples spread her fragrance

Admiring the beauty at White Emperor City

Her wonderful dance vividly embodies the spirit

After satisfying my curiosity, I asked many questions

Feeling the times and touching upon events, my lament increased

The late emperor's maids numbered eighty

Gongsun's sword dance was the foremost

Fifty years passed in the blink of an eye

The world was turned upside down, the royal court darkened

Disciples of the Pear Garden scattered like smoke

The lingering beauty of female musicians reflected in the cold sun

South of Golden Millet Mound, the trees are already large

In Qutang Stone City, grass is mixed with sadness

The banquet of tortoiseshell, the urgent pipes, the melody ends again

Joy ends and sorrow comes, the moon rises in the east

The old man does not know where to go

Wandering in the desolate mountains, his sorrow deepens

Drunken Song on Stone Fish Lake

Stone Fish Lake is like Dongting Lake

Summer water is full, Mount Jun is green

The mountain is the wine vessel, the water is the wine pond

Wine drinkers sit on the islands one by one

The long wind makes big waves for days

Cannot stop people from transporting wine by boat

I hold a long ladle, sitting in Baqiu

Pouring wine for all around to dispel sorrow

Shenbao Local Supplement Film Special

[Everyone, Don't Misunderstand] Mae West's Solemn Statement (Continued) 250

— Yang Yang

It's almost unbelievable that a woman who uses sex appeal on stage or screen to attract audiences has many aspects of her private life that even old-fashioned housewives can't fully achieve. But that is an undeniable fact. She often says to people: [When it comes to my private life, I am not afraid to compare it with any woman's private life.] She has been in Hollywood for three years, but a group of nosy, gossipy reporters have yet to find anything objectionable about her. If you still don't believe she is one of Hollywood's most forward-thinking puritans, we can examine many of the sins of 1934 one by one to see which sin can be pinned on Mae West. Some say that stealing someone else's husband is this year's most hateful sin. But Mae West doesn't even look at other people's husbands. She has said: [Other women's men, whether they are husbands, fiancés, or boyfriends, I will never compete with others for them. Of course, men who have already divorced their wives are included in this. Although love is similar to war, and all is fair in war, there is intense competition in love, but you must remember that there are plenty of single men in the world for you to choose from, so why steal someone else's property?]

Or spreading rumors is now the second biggest sin. Even first-class stars cannot avoid whispering about the secrets of their rival stars with friends. But Mae West is most opposed to interfering in other people's privacy. She treats people fairly and is especially loyal to all her old friends. She herself has said: [Whoever wants to tell me bad things about my friends, I will definitely not believe them. Conversely, I will never say bad things about others to others. I know from my personal experience that that is the most unfair thing. Since I came to Hollywood, I don't know how many bad things have been published in the newspapers. They are all baseless. The first thing is that they always say I have a husband. I have protested so much that I don't want to protest anymore.] Therefore, she hates those who spread rumors the most, and when she sees friends whispering and acting suspiciously, she always walks away and has never participated in it once.

Snobbery and fickleness are also common problems among many stars. They avoid their old friends who were very close to them before they became famous, or who contributed to them, or who helped them, after they become rich. Mae West is not that kind of snob. Many actors who were famous on stage or screen but later failed are still constantly being helped by her. One of them, a once very famous singer, is still being provided with living expenses by Mae and lives in Hollywood.

Other minor sins, such as hypocrisy and pretense, are especially difficult for ordinary stars to avoid. But Mae, some say, she may be the most honest woman in Hollywood. Her own way of observing this matter is: [I do a beautiful thing, a smart thing, not because that thing is beautiful or smart. I follow what my heart likes and seek what my heart finds peace in. Conversely, many people think that beautiful things should be done, but I refuse to do them because my nature is not close to them. For example, opera, I have never liked to watch it. If someone sincerely likes to watch opera, that's another matter, but among the people who go to watch opera, some of them don't really like it, but want to show their faces in the opera house and let people see them and think they are beautiful. As far as I am concerned, I like to watch boxing, I don't care what people say, I will go to see it if I want to.] Similarly, Mae refuses to participate in all unnecessary social events, regardless of whether they affect her career. She has never [used political tactics]. She has never used strikes to threaten to get a raise. She doesn't think rebellion is something she does. She also has no laziness, which is the greatest sin. Whenever she is not working on the set, her time is spent on writing. She writes novels, plays, and songs. She also practices singing every day. She never goes to nightclubs to play and does not do boring things to kill time. Finally, her courage is admirable. After her jewelry was stolen, she received many threatening letters, telling her not to report it, otherwise her life would be in danger. But she eventually reported it and personally testified in court. So the judge also said: [If everyone were as brave and decisive as Mae West, half of the evils in the world could be reduced. (The End)

Film Commentary

Review of [The Barretts of Wimpole Street] 251

— Ling He

The Barretts of Wimpole Street — Nanjing

Naturally, a film like this is very worthy of praise. At the very least, we can glimpse the high level of development of American cinematic art.

To have a deeper understanding of this film, we cannot ignore the dynamics of society during the Victorian era. After the Industrial Revolution, the early capitalist ideology began to contend with established forces, which is an explanation of historical significance. Regarding the poet couple Robert Browning and Elizabeth Barrett, during their youth, they suffered the cruel poison of feudal forces. They consciously became rebels against feudalism, and at the same time, they saw to some extent the painful cries of the laborers. In particular, from [The Cry of the Children], we can know that Elizabeth was indeed a timid awakener. Of course, to be precise, in that era, they were not yet advanced poets, but they were not lagging behind either.

From this perspective, we see the playwright writing Elizabeth as a timid woman who opposes feudalism, escaping from the violence of her family (her father) and longing for freedom with Browning. In any case, it touches reality. Here we see Sidney Franklin, in addition to positive depictions, also used symbolic techniques. For example, Barrett (i.e., Elizabeth's father) repeatedly closes the windows, darkening the room. He imprisons his daughter. Elizabeth struggles to run to the window, smiling at the winter sun. Furthermore, after her joyful meeting with Browning, we see how he positively describes the strong and cruel feudal forces, and how he depicts the ferocity of that domestic tyrant: When Barrett enters the door, a puppy immediately flees to its original place. The third daughter, Henrietta, and her lover meet secretly in the snow, looking so pitiful. When Barrett discovers that his third daughter is in love, he brutally threatens her not to associate with that officer again. When Barrett forces Elizabeth to leave Browning and return to her room, the director uses a bird's-eye view.

In addition to the above, we might as well look at his depiction of the passionate love of young poets. Isn't it so? A young girl needs love after all, and the chains of family cannot bind the passionate love of a young girl. Like what Browning said, [I love you, I can never leave you], Elizabeth and Browning being engaged, her chronic illness suddenly healed, she said: [I cannot die, I do not want to die]. She began to be active in life, for the glory of love. This is a great contrast to her seeing the dim moonlight and the dripping rain outside the window and crying desperately. Similarly, the third daughter, Henrietta, also has the determination to sacrifice for love. Here we can see that the author has emphasized the part of love very much. Regarding this part, the excellent scenes include Browning entering the bedroom and Elizabeth tidying up the bedding in great surprise, and the tenderness of the joyful conversation in the park, all of which are very good depictions.

However, in our demand for realism, does this film very accurately depict the reality of the time in cinematic art? We feel it is still quite insufficient. If the playwright was a courageous realist, he would have focused heavily on the clash of new and old ideas, bravely demonstrating the glory of opposing feudalism. However, it has intensified the depiction of Barrett's perverted personality. He made Barrett forbid his daughter from marrying entirely because of his hatred of love due to his own wife's elopement. At the same time, he added a desire beyond father-daughter love between the father and daughter. As a result, the reason why the father opposed his daughter's marriage was not emphasizing the conflict between new and old ideologies.

Of course, we do not say that there are no such fathers in the world, but this is not the most prominent representative of the general, that is, it is definitely not a typical depiction. Therefore, due to the emphasis on this aspect, it weakens the positive depiction of opposing feudalism, which is inevitably a pity; although I will not ignore the fact that the feudal Barrett borrowed the power of religion to extremely oppress his children, causing their positive reaction.

Needless to say, the highest level of development of film art in the United States is unfolded here, which is a kind of amazing brilliance. This is of course because the director Franklin's technique is too good, and every actor can express himself as he wishes, not to mention the beauty of the photography. Strictly speaking, I think Maureen O'Sullivan, who plays the third daughter, is above Fredric March in acting.

Review of [The Dragon Pool Key] 252

— You Jing

First of all, because we have recently been shown several detective films in succession, and most of them are mediocre and vulgar, simply boring detective films, we must specifically say a few words about this type of film.

Originally, because the detective story itself is full of drama, under a more serious attitude and clever techniques, it is possible to construct extremely perfect and meaningful works. The so-called meaning here should be placed on the intellectual education of thinking scientifically about unusual events and seeking solutions.

But what kind of detective films have we seen recently? From [Corpse in the Empty Building], [San Francisco Trunk Murder Case], and [Corpse in the Foggy Night], to this [Dragon Pool Key], whether in terms of results or significance, the distance from what we hope for in detective films and the level that detective films should and can achieve is too far. Originally, in the hands of filmmakers who regard movies as one of the pastimes for the well-fed and well-clothed, and who do not need any art other than [business]—even if they do, they only need to make the pastime better and more enjoyable—the vulgarity of film works is of course not expressed solely in the area of detective films. Isn't it so? Forcibly arranging a case, forcibly coming up with a solution, and then forcefully inserting a love component between men and women, in order to alleviate the dull atmosphere after death, injury, and robbery, isn't it enough for the leisurely to pass two hours?

Speaking of [The Dragon Pool Key] itself, it is not much different from the detective films that were shown before it. It's just that the former used indoor mechanisms, boxes, cars, airplanes, etc. as the key to the story, but this [Dragon Pool Key] has replaced it with a gloomy ancient pool as the main background of the script, in order to use the actors' swimming skills and strong bodies to give some viewers a little satisfaction. As for using a key as a tool for solving the case, it is no different from other films using something else.

Detective films are originally known for their particularity, bizarre events, tortuous process, and rigorous structure. This film also narrates the events that are enough to develop into a murder case due to money, love, etc., but in the plot, we do not see at all that the murderer has the necessity to kill. The necessary twists, tension, and changes are not fully present here either.

Detective star Warren William in this film, just as the content of the film determines him, does not have the ability to express the unique characteristics of a great detective. The rest of the actors are just average, and they are considered competent for such a script.

A Bouquet of Flowers from Happy Woods 253

— Gao Mei

After [The Virtuous Wife] was publicly screened in the two major theaters of Central and Shanghai, the photos of child star Zhang Lingling requested by donors have reached more than 30.

Xu Suzhen is actively practicing a song called [Remnant Flower Song] in [Three Daughters-in-Law].

Bai Ye, the protagonist of [Three Daughters-in-Law], went home to visit relatives a week ago and has not returned. There is still a bit of acting waiting for her to reshoot!

[Madness] is Xu Liang's attempt at a new movie. It is a tragedy similar to [Goodbye, Shanghai!].

The rumor that Wang Tianbei has left Happy Woods is absolutely untrue. Wang is planning to continue his efforts in Happy Woods, or will direct a sound film.

Happy Woods' sound production is in active progress.

Movie Novel

Black-Faced Compassion (Imitation of Life) (5) 254

— Wen Yin

Since that stormy day, not many years have passed, and Beatrice has become famous throughout the country, known as the Pancake Queen of America, and Delilah's face, printed on every bag of pancake flour, has become the high standard of a great business. Delilah herself is very detached from money. Except for the future of Peola, and her own affairs after death, she almost doesn't know what money is for. She only seeks to serve her beloved Miss Pei. She insists on cooking three meals a day for herself and Miss Pei. Pei understands her loyalty and had already deposited a sum of money in the bank under Delilah's name. That sum of money is already enough to make Delilah economically independent and have more than enough, as long as she wants to enjoy that kind of independence herself. Of course, Pei also did not forget that great contributor, Elmer Smith. ... Time flies, and suddenly recalls the tenth anniversary of the occurrence of Delilah pancake flour. Pei specially held a banquet in the Sutton house. Elmer was the chairman of the bar that day. Pei was surrounded by men who envied her. She was wearing a gorgeous evening dress, truly radiant, making her figure even more slender and her skin more delicate. After a while, Beatrice escaped the men surrounding her and ran to the balcony to get some air. She wanted to be alone for a while. The place where she stood was directly opposite the front door. She saw a person pacing back and forth outside the door, as if looking for something. He suddenly looked up and saw Pei's shadow. He stared for a while, then suddenly smiled and asked; [It's funny, how can't I find the doorbell. Do you know, where did that thing go?] As he was talking, the gate suddenly opened, and a guest walked out, brushing shoulders with him as he went down. The person who wanted to come in nodded to Pei with a smile and said: [Okay, okay, I can come in.] Pei felt very strange, she walked down and asked the doorman who the stranger was, but the doorman didn't know either. She wanted to avoid him, he seemed to be coming in to find someone. But as soon as she turned her head, the first guest was already standing in front of her. She treated him as if he were an old friend, and greeted her unceremoniously: [Hello... I'm in.] Pei was stunned by his greeting. She stammered: [Oh, you're in.] The man said again: [It's very strange, where is that doorbell, do you know? I'm afraid that doorbell must be inlaid with gold and copper, so the owner hides it in the safe at night. One day, I'll come during the day to see what the doorbell looks like.] Pei couldn't help but laugh when she heard him say this. This person, she felt, had a special flavor... almost like... champagne. So they started talking like old acquaintances. When the music started, the two of them felt extremely natural to hug and dance. Pei only found out his name was Stephen Archer while dancing with him. He was Elmer's friend, and Elmer asked him to meet Beatrice today. After one dance, Stephen went to get ice water for Pei. At this time, Elmer had found him. Elmer followed behind Stephen, as if arguing with him about something. Only Stephen was heard saying: [I told you I don't have time to meet her, Elmer. I'm busy now.] At this time, the two of them had already walked in front of Beatrice. Elmer grabbed Stephen and said: [Haha she's here... you come and see her, whether you want to or not] Stephen looked up at Beatrice's face, unable to speak for a long time. Suddenly he laughed wildly: [Oh... oh... oh... oh... so you are...] Pei couldn't wait to finish speaking, and continued: [Pancake flour king.] As she said this, she laughed out loud too. Elmer looked at Pei, then at Stephen, and then asked: [What? Did you know each other before?] But Pei didn't say anything, and pushed him away. (To be continued)
